<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction-to-entrepreneurship">INTRODUCTION TO ENTREPRENEURSHIP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-to-entrepreneurship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition-of-terms">Definition of Terms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-terms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition-of-an-entrepreneur">Definition of an entrepreneur<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-an-entrepreneur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>☑ An entrepreneur is a person who identifies a business opportunity, harnesses and obtains the resources necessary to initiate a successful business activity.
☑ The entrepreneur implements the idea
☑ Undertakes to operate the business
☑ An entrepreneur is therefore a central key individual in the society who makes things happens for economic development.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="entrepreneurship-meaning">Entrepreneurship meaning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entrepreneurship-meaning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>☑ In the broader sense entrepreneurship refers to the means of stimulating innovative and creative undertakings for a better business community or world.
☑ The act or process of identifying business opportunities and gathering the necessary resources to initiate a successful business activity.
☑ Entrepreneurship is a French word meaning to undertake and focuses on a business enterprise
☑ Entrepreneurship can exist in any situation – therefore it is the creation of values through establishing a business enterprise.
☑ Entrepreneurship means having an idea of one’s own and trying to implement the idea to create values on it.
☑ Entrepreneurship is a term which encompasses what entrepreneurs do i.e
☐ Identifying a business opportunity of a particular demand
☐ Look at the opportunity as a process of creating, something that did not exist.
☐ Constantly searching/ harnessing ones environment and resources to implement the activities.
☐ Creating a totally new product and using it in as new.
☑ Entrepreneurship there is the practice of starting a new business or revitalizing existing businesses in response to identifying opportunities.</p>
<p>Page 4 of 165</p>
<p>Self-Employment</p>
<ul>
<li>Working independently and earning a living from it.</li>
<li>This is a concept that arises when the entrepreneur relies on revenues from his business as a source of income</li>
<li>What is Unemployment? Advantages and disadvantages of Self Employment?</li>
<li>What is Salaried Employment? Advantages and Disadvantages of Salaried employment? Enterprise</li>
<li>A business undertaking by an individual for the purpose of making a profit.</li>
</ul>
<p>Factors impeding the growth of Entrepreneurship</p>
<ul>
<li>High Taxation Levels</li>
<li>Corruption and Official Harassment</li>
<li>Unregulated competition from outside countries</li>
<li>Decline in personal incomes</li>
<li>The high cost of finance</li>
<li>Lack of entrepreneurial culture</li>
<li>Poor transport and communication networks</li>
<li>Lack of skills and knowledge</li>
<li>Explain the distinctions between an Entrepreneur and a Manager</li>
</ul>
<p>Contribution of Entrepreneurship to National Development</p>
<ul>
<li>The economic growth, the improved quality of life, the equitable distribution of resources and the capacity of the economy to deal with economic, social and environmental development.</li>
<li>Main objectives of national development include:</li>
<li>Provide basic needs to every citizen: food, shelter, health, security, education, clothing</li>
<li>Elimination / Reduction of poverty: reduce rural-urban migration</li>
<li>Provision of opportunities for employment and personal advancement</li>
<li>Trying to narrow the income differences between the rich and the poor.</li>
</ul>
<p>i) Employment Creation:
ii) Promotion of National Productivity: This is through production of goods and services within the country and therefore they contribute to the Gross Domestic Product (GDP)
iii) Raising Standards of Living: It’s measured by the capacity of people of a country to buy goods and services. Entrepreneurs contribute by employing people and giving them salaries or wages to buy their necessities.
iv) Conservation of foreign Exchange: Entrepreneurs produce goods and services that are needed by people and reduction in importing those goods and hence the government saves foreign exchange.
v) Export Promotion: Entrepreneurs who produce goods and services for export earn
vi) Conservation Agent: Entrepreneurs can contribute to conservation and utilization of resources e.g. manufacturing a Jiko that uses sawdust instead of wood charcoal
vii) Rural development which in effect.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="entrepreneurship">Entrepreneurship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entrepreneurship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>i) Entrepreneurship looks at particular individuals in a business set-up. It operates in large business or organization which is business minded to make profit.
ii) Entrepreneurs operate autonomously for the welfare of the organization.
iii) The term Intra – refers to within – therefore Entrepreneurship is a process whereby an individual or group within a large organization creates something new or different to maximize on the available opportunities to that organization. iv) Intra can therefore be equated to entra within the context of a large organization where the workers are a leeway to be creative or innovative on their own.
v) They become competitive, socially and economically the idea is to allow individuals within the organization to act and think independently.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-functions-of-an-entrepreneur">The Functions of an Entrepreneur<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-functions-of-an-entrepreneur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) The bearing of uncertainty is the primary function of the entrepreneur i.e. losses or profits.
ii) The management of the business enterprise ie can delegate iii) Provision of risk capital and invention.
iv) Identifying gaps in the market and turning such gaps to business opportunities i.e to initiate a business.
v) Financing the businesses, through raising and mobilizing the necessary resources to exploit opportunity.
vi) Searching for business opportunities through environmental scans. vii) Mobilization of resources needed to start and run a business e.g. from</p>
<p>a) Personal savings
b) Friends &amp; relatives
c) Financial institutions e.t.c</p>
<p>viii) Evaluation of business opportunities to access viability and any other benefits that might accrue to the business.
ix) Provide the necessary leadership for the business and those working in it.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-entrepreneurship">Advantages of Entrepreneurship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-entrepreneurship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>i.) Financial gains

iii.) Provide job opportunities to the unemployed or those seeking better jobs.

vi.) Facilitates competition encouraging high quality products
vii.) Facilitates production of more goods and services
viii.) Leads to the development of newer markets

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-evolution-of-entrepreneurship">2. EVOLUTION OF ENTREPRENEURSHIP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-evolution-of-entrepreneurship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-evolution-of-entrepreneurship-in-kenya">The Evolution of Entrepreneurship in Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-evolution-of-entrepreneurship-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Interest in the development of entrepreneurship and small enterprise in Kenya gained momentum as a possible remedy to the stagnation of economic development and the escalating unemployment problem between the early 1960 and 1970s</li>
<li>Although there were attempts by the government to develop entrepreneurship, the main impetus came from the international labor organization (ILO) report.</li>
<li>The report centered on the potential of the informal sector and suggested that the bulk of Kenya's urban workers were self-employed in small enterprises.</li>
<li>The report proposed that the development of this sector could;</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>i.Promote employment ii.Facilitate development iii.Facilitate equitable distribution of resources.</p>
<p>☑ Based on this report the government responded with a seasonal paper in 1973 – which recognized the role of entrepreneurship in employment creation not just in the informal sector but also in the formal sector.
☑ Subsequent development plans have devoted time to the development of strategies and to promote small-scale enterprises and entrepreneurs which include.  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>∘</mo></mrow><annotation class="mord">∘</span></span></span></span></span> The industrial estate programme  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">∘</span></span></span></span></span> Establishment of development agents e.g ICDC and KIE <div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="economic-social-and-political-factors-affecting-entrepreneurial-development">Economic, Social and Political Factors Affecting Entrepreneurial Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#economic-social-and-political-factors-affecting-entrepreneurial-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) High taxation levels. For business and personal incomes</p>
<p>☑ Which in effect reduce profits earned making it un-attractive to engage in business
☑ Taxation of raw materials and other inputs raise production costs.</p>
<p>b) Corruption and official harassment</p>
<p>☑ Occurs where entrepreneurs are forced to bribe officials in various government departments to allow operation or start up.
☑ Raids under one pretext or another which tends to be very harassing.</p>
<p>c) Unregulated competition from the outside world due.</p>
<p>☑ Liberalization which opened importation competing locally produced goods.</p>
<p>d) Declining personal incomes of people due to</p>
<p>☑ Over-increasing cost of living
☑ Arise in unemployment</p>
<p>e) The high cost of finance</p>
<p>☑ The cost of borrowing is high
☑ Business collapses because they lack ability to repay loans.</p>
<p>f) Lack of necessary skills and knowledge due to</p>
<p>☑ lack of training opportunities
☑ high education costs</p>
<p>g) Poor transport and communication network</p>
<p>☑ making business difficult
☑ Inconveniencing consumers
☑ High energy costs
☑ Lack of entrepreneurial culture</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="myths-associated-with-entrepreneurship">Myths Associated with Entrepreneurship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#myths-associated-with-entrepreneurship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Entrepreneurs are doers not thinkers: Although it is true entrepreneurs tend towards action, they are also thinkers.</li>
<li>Entrepreneurs are born not made: The idea that the characteristics of entrepreneurs cannot be taught or learned, that they have innate trait, has long been prevalent. Today, however, the recognition of entrepreneurship as a discipline is helping to dispel the myth.</li>
</ol>
<p>Page 9 of 165

Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Entrepreneurs are always inventors: entrepreneurship covers more than just invention. It requires a complete understanding of innovative behavior in all forms.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Entrepreneurs are academic and social misfits. The belief that entrepreneurs are academically and socially ineffective is as a result of some business owners having started successful enterprise after dropping out of school or quitting a job. Today the entrepreneur is considered a hero socially, economically and academically and no longer misfit.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Entrepreneurs must fit the profile many books and articles have presented checklist of characteristics of a successful entrepreneur. Today we realize that a standard entrepreneurial profile</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All entrepreneurs need to run a business successful is money: Many business fail because of managerial incompetence, lack of financial understanding, poor planning etc. To many entrepreneurs money is a source but not an end in itself.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All entrepreneurs need is luck. Being at “the right place at the right time” is always an advantage. But luck happens when preparation meets opportunity as an equally appropriate advantage. Prepared entrepreneurs who seize the opportunity when it arises often seem “Lucky” they are in fact simply better prepared to deal with situations and turn them into success. What appears to be luck really is preparation, determination, desire, knowledge and innovativeness?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Entrepreneurs must fail; in fact failure can teach many lessons to those willing to learn and often leads to future successes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Entrepreneurs are extremely risk takers (Gamblers). Entrepreneur is usually working on a moderate or calculated risk.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It takes a lot of money to start a business. This is false because it is all about using the little resources to make the most out of it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Those who make it are those with rich backups. You can start from scratch with no special favors or advantages and succeed</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Some people go about thinking that banks do not lend to those who wish to start up businesses.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Those who start business, do so in very attractive industries</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All entrepreneurs are rich and have financial success</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Starting a business is easy. It is difficult and getting it running takes a lot.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="theories-of-entrepreneurship">Theories of entrepreneurship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theories-of-entrepreneurship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The theories that explains entrepreneurship include:</p>
<p>a) Psychological Theory
b) Motivational Theory
c) Sociological Theory
d) Economic Theory
e) The Resource Based Theory
f) Competence Based Theory</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>g) Heterogeneous Demand Theory</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="psychological-theory">Psychological theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychological-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The focus is that entrepreneurs have unique values, attitudes and need which drive them.</li>
<li>People’s behavior results from their attempts to satisfy their unique needs and values.</li>
<li>The psychological school focuses on personality factors believing that entrepreneurs have unique values and attitudes towards work and life.</li>
<li>Among the most frequent traits of entrepreneurs include the Need for achievement, Locus of Control and Risk taking propensity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="motivational-theory">Motivational Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#motivational-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Motivation is that which causes you to behave in the way you behave i.e. the why of behavior</li>
<li>Entrepreneurial motivation is those factors and forces or events that energizes an individual, his desires and the needs to go into and sustain a business venture.</li>
<li>Types of motivation; i) Internal Motivation Factors ii) External Motivation Factors</li>
<li>Internal Motivations and Drives</li>
</ul>
<p>✓ Refers to those personal traits and desires that induce a person to become an entrepreneur. Such motivations are;</p>
<p>i. Employment Creation Need.
ii. Need for independence or self-Reliance: iii. Need for Power:
iv. Need for Recognition:
v. Need for Security:
vi. Self-actualization need:</p>
<p>□ External Motivations and Drives</p>
<p>i. Infrastructure:
ii. Credit Facilities: iii. Information Support iv. Pricing Policy v. Tax Policy vi. Legal Control vii. Political Climate viii. Technical Technology Assistance ix. Training Consultancy Assistance x. Friends Motivation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="658cd14f">Maslow’s Need Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#658cd14f" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Theory of human needs is identified with the psychologist Abraham Maslow. This theory is based on three specific assumptions:</p>
<ol>
<li>The human beings are never satisfied. Their wants are determined by what they have. When people are hungry or thirsty, the quest for food or water influences how they behave. However if food and water is acquired, the same person will want something else, perhaps a safe place to live in or a social status.</li>
<li>A satisfied need does not cause behavior. Once people satisfy their need for safety, they are motivated by yet unsatisfied needs, not the ones – that are satisfied,</li>
<li>Human needs are arranged in hierarchy of importance. These needs range from low level biological (physiological) needs to such high level needs as self-actualization.</li>
</ol>
<p>Page 11 of 165
This document is available on

Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-07a6e172.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>Self – Actualization Needs (Desire to fulfil our potential)</p>
<p>Esteem Needs (awareness of importance of ourselves)</p>
<p>Belongingness Needs (Desire for friendship and happiness)</p>
<p>Safety Needs (Desire for security from present and future</p>
<p>Physiological needs (food, clothing, shelter)</p>
<p>Discus Impetus for entrepreneurship. Discus factors that propel people to self-employment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-affecting-entrepreneurial-development">Factors Affecting Entrepreneurial Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-affecting-entrepreneurial-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="political-factors">Political Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#political-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>☑ Political environment is concerned with the policies pursued by the government. Components of political environment include; ☐ The political stability ☐ Political system e.g.</p>
<p>i. Capitalism: whereby the means of production are owned by individuals. A capitalist is a wealthy merchant who uses his/her money to invest in trade for profit.</p>
<p>ii. Socialist: means of production are owned by government iii. Market economy: whereby means of production are owned by government and individuals.</p>
<p>☐ Political climate being favorable ☐ Policies</p>
<p>pursued by the government: e.g.</p>
<ul>
<li>Changes in monetary and fiscal policy</li>
<li>Policies concerning price and wage control</li>
<li>Policies concerning nationalization</li>
</ul>
<p>☑ Economic Factors: Concerned with factors that affect consumers purchasing power and spending patterns:</p>
<ul>
<li>Inflation: increase in prices of goods and services without a corresponding increase in output.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>○ Money supply: Quantity of money in circulation which is supplied by Central Bank
○ Interest Rates: rate charged by commercial banks on the money that it lends
○ Exchange rates and controls
○ Taxes and subsidies (Incentives given to encourage production of good or service)
○ Income levels</p>
<p>✓ Social Cultural Factors
○ Is made up of institutions and other forces that affect a society’s basic values, perceptions, preferences and behaviors. People grow up in a particular society that shapes their basic beliefs and values.
○ Social factors e.g. family, religion, social roles and status, reference groups
○ Cultural factors like values, beliefs, customs and lifestyle.</p>
<p>✓ Technological Factors. Ways and means of production</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-entrepreneur">THE ENTREPRENEUR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-entrepreneur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-entrepreneurs">Types of Entrepreneurs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-entrepreneurs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-craft-entrepreneurs">a) Craft entrepreneurs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-craft-entrepreneurs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ Exploits and utilizes personal skills to start a business without thinking of its growth or the expansion objectives
✓ Often times than not in this type of entrepreneurship;
i. There is no expanding even after a long time
ii. It is not business expansion oriented.
iii. The skills can be technical skills, professional skill e.t.c</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-opportunistic-entrepreneurs">b) Opportunistic entrepreneurs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-opportunistic-entrepreneurs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ This is a person who starts a business, acts as a manager and with a view to expand the business to maximum.
✓ He might not have the skill or profession but he has the opportunity to start and direct others.
✓ He sees beyond and has abilities to initiate and venture into business that will expand and grow.
✓ He is innovative i.e. somebody able to delegate activities to others, ready and able to see, scan the environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="c-social-entrepreneur">c) Social entrepreneur<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-social-entrepreneur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ Recognizes a social problem and uses entrepreneurial principles to organize, create and manage a venture to achieve social change.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="d-political-entrepreneur">d) Political entrepreneur<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-political-entrepreneur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ Is a business person who utilizes political systems or seeks support from political bodies in order to promote, expand and profit from their own commercial ventures.
✓ Apolitical player who seeks to gain certain political and social benefits in return for providing the common goods that can be shared by an organized general public. e) High Tech:</p>

<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> New technological developments have created opportunities for those with the right technical expertise</p>
<p>f) Concept Multipliers</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Someone who identifies a successful concept that can be duplicated by others eg</p>
<p>g) Acquirer :</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Those who take over a business started by others and use their own ideas to make it successful</p>
<p>h) Buy/Sell artists: those who buy a company for the purpose of improving it before selling it for a profit.</p>
<p>i) Economy of Scale exploiters: Those who benefit from large volume of sales by offering discount prices and operating with low overheads.</p>
<p>j) Inventors: Those with particular inventive abilities who design a better product and then create companies to develop, produce and sell the item.</p>
<p>k) Self-employed: individuals who perform all the work and keep all the profit.</p>
<p>l) Speculator/Value: Those individuals who buy property at a low price with the anticipation that prices will go up and sell at a higher price.</p>
<p>m) Conglomerate: an entrepreneur who builds up a portfolio of ownership in small businesses, sometimes using shares or assets of one company to provide the financial base to acquire another.</p>
<p>n) Matriarch or patriarch: The head of family owned business who often employs several members of the family.</p>
<p>Characteristic/Traits of a Potential Entrepreneur</p>
<p>a) Initiative and risks taken by;</p>

<p>g) Systematic planning;

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Sticks with own judgment in the face of opposition or early lack of success <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> confronts problems and issues directly <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Tells others what they have to do.</p>
<p>i) Persuasion;
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> convinces people to buy the products or service

<p>j) Uses strategic influence and networking;
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> To develop business contact

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Risk taker, Mobilizer, Marketer, Financier, Shareholder, Director, Initiator</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-to-consider-in-starting-a-business">Factors to consider in starting a business<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-to-consider-in-starting-a-business" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Personal Factors</p>
<p>i. Personal abilities</p>
<p>One must have personality traits that will enable him/her to start, continue and succeed in business. One must have entrepreneurial traits and be motivated and determined to succeed in business. E.g. one must be willing to work hard and pursue his/her goals persistently he/she must be innovative, creative and optimistic. ii. Skills: One needs to have the training and experience necessary in the proposed line of</p>
<p>Page 15 of 165
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>business. He/she must have adequate knowledge about product or service and the necessary managerial skills for the business to succeed.</p>
<p>iii. Interests / hobbies: As an entrepreneur, how much interests does one have in line of his/her business? Ann interest or hobby can be a basis for a business.</p>
<p>iv. Family: Small businesses and family are inseparable, one affects the other. You need to consider possible effects of the business on the family and how the family could affect the business.</p>
<p>v. Health: Running a business successfully calls for a lot of hard work. It involves a lot of physical and mental energies. If an entrepreneur has failing health, it is advisable to engage in less strenuous activities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-resource-factors">b) Resource Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-resource-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i.) Financial Resources: These include money saved by the entrepreneur and money that may be borrowed from individuals and institutions like banks, building societies, cooperatives, etc to start and run a business.</p>
<p>ii.) Labor Resources: The availability and suitability of labour should be assessed.</p>
<p>iii.) Equipment/Machinery: Tools of the trade that are essential in any business. They may include furniture, office equipment, machine for a specific job, etc.</p>
<p>iv.) Raw Materials: These are items that are to be converted to states that can be readily used by consumers. These include timber if one is furniture business, cloth materials if in dress making business.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-environmental-factors">c) Environmental factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-environmental-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i.) Location: Factors such as community profile, communication, road, water, safety, source of raw materials and competition should be considered when locating a business. This enables easy accessibility of the business by customers.</p>
<p>ii.) Government Policies / regulations: Policies such as taxation, pricing, licensing, loans and policy documents affect small enterprises. Information on the above is available from district Information Offices, Trade Organizations, Kenya Chamber of Commerce and Government Printers. iii.) Infrastructure: Availability of roads, power, water and telephone services are very important in some types of business.</p>
<p>iv.) The economy of the society: The average income and employment trends determine the demand for goods and services within the community to sell products or services at reduced profits, a strong economy creates ample demand and good profits.</p>
<p>v.) Competition: An entrepreneur should try to assess the number of competitors in his or her environment in order to compete with them successful.</p>
<p>vi.) Market: A market for the product or services is very important to the entrepreneur. One has to assess whether there's a steady market.</p>
<p>vii.) Community and Culture: The entrepreneur has to consider:</p>
<p>a) General Customs of the region eg customs about mode of dressing
b) The mix of politics
c) Taboos / beliefs eg Muslims cannot operate any business dealing with pork products
d) Traditions peculiar to his / her community</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="creativity-and-innovation">CREATIVITY AND INNOVATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#creativity-and-innovation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Creativity refers to the process of devising a new idea, or thing that result in the improved efficiency or effectiveness of a system.</li>
<li>Innovation means improving an existing idea or thing. Commercializing of an idea or turning idea into an opportunity.</li>
<li>Innovation builds on creativity when something new, tangible and value-creating is developed from the ideas.</li>
<li>Innovation turns new concepts into realities, creating wealth and power.</li>
<li>Creative destruction occurs when innovations make long-standing arrangement obsolete and frees resources to be employed else where leading to greater economic efficiency. E.g. computerization.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reasons-for-opposing-innovation">Reasons for Opposing Innovation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reasons-for-opposing-innovation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) The entrepreneurs tend to have a practical concern that unforeseen innovation may cause a disaster e.g. side effects e.g. of a drug.
ii) Fear of losing profits in the event innovation does not translate to the expectations.
iii) Where the entrepreneur held a monopoly position in the market, there is fear of losing authority and control.
iv) Fear of upsetting the moral and social value of demand for the product. v) Desire to preserve the existing market confidence vi) Fear of upsetting tradition in production management and market scope.
vii) Fear of opening a loophole to competition hence loss of business grip.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reasons-for-innovation">Reasons for Innovation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reasons-for-innovation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Innovation is essential for the entrepreneur in solving the inefficiency problems.</li>
<li>As a means of cost reduction and imposing significance social and market grip.</li>
<li>Profit improvements are looked at from the innovation point of view though newer technology in management and production.</li>
<li>To encounter competition by already established businesses.</li>
<li>To facilitate opening up of new markets both locally and internationally.</li>
<li>To facilitate diversification of products risks and losses. ✓ To protect current position of monopoly or success.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-2-4-requirements-of-innovation">1.2.4 Requirements of Innovation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-2-4-requirements-of-innovation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i.) Economic demand</p>
<ul>
<li>People engage in innovation out of belief that the economic returns will be greater than its costs.</li>
</ul>
<p>ii.) Surplus capital</p>
<ul>
<li>provides the necessary time and startup costs for implementing a new idea. iii.) Ability to assemble and invest capital.</li>
</ul>
<p>iv.) Mobile capital which is stable.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-entrepreneurship-culture">THE ENTREPRENEURSHIP CULTURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-entrepreneurship-culture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="culture-definition">Culture Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#culture-definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Culture is defined as a set of values, perceptions wants and behavior learned by a member of a society from family and other institutions</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Weber argues that “Protestantism encourages a culture which emphasizes individualism, achievement motivation, legislation of entrepreneurial vocations, rationality and self – reliance.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Hosted – defines culture as a collective programming of the mind which distinguishes the member of one group or category of people from another.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="entrepreneurial-culture">Entrepreneurial Culture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entrepreneurial-culture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Refers to the way of embracing the concept of finding new opportunities in business and gathering the necessary resources to fill the opportunity.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Many governments around the world want to promote entrepreneurship because they have recognized the importance of entrepreneurship.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> In other words entrepreneurial culture is a way of people embarrassing life by participating in activities that enable them create new business enterprises.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> A country can develop the entrepreneurial culture by forming policies that constitute the following;</p>
<ul>
<li>Integration of entrepreneurship training in the overall education system to tap on youths</li>
<li>Exposure of entrepreneurship to those who look potential to actual business practices and activities through the networks and business contacts of rule models.</li>
<li>Creation of a conducive and enabling environment that permits new business to immerge and flourish.</li>
</ul>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The creation of entrepreneurial culture has to come from deep social convictions based on strong values and systems of the locals</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It should be created in a way that it welcomes entrepreneurship and respects the investor and also reflecting the core values</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="importance-of-entrepreneurship-culture">Importance of Entrepreneurship Culture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#importance-of-entrepreneurship-culture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>i. Enhances economic growth and building of social capital. ii. Enhances job creation. iii. Acts as a primary source of innovation. iv. Helps in the devolution of government power for policy implementation. v. Direct influence development in tech. H/R capital formation e.t.c.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-cultural-habits-that-promote-entrepreneurial-development">The cultural habits that promote entrepreneurial development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-cultural-habits-that-promote-entrepreneurial-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-money-orientation">a) Money orientation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-money-orientation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="b-future-orientation">b) Future orientation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-future-orientation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<li>A society that has foresight to know about the future business environment is likely to have more entrepreneurs.</li>
<li>This is because they are likely to visualize key changes that are likely to create opportunity.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="c-time-consciousness">c) Time consciousness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-time-consciousness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Knowledge that time exists and its importance</li>
<li>Knowing the right time to start an entrepreneurial activity.</li>
<li>Utilization of time</li>
<li>The correct timing of the market conditions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="d-trust-and-honesty">d) Trust and honesty<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-trust-and-honesty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Through trust consumer demand is gained on the products and services available.</li>
<li>Entrepreneurs should reciprocate this by ensuring honesty by providing the expected standards.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="e-hard-work-i-e">e) Hard work i.e<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-hard-work-i-e" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-cultural-factors-inhibiting-entrepreneurial-development">The cultural factors inhibiting entrepreneurial development.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-cultural-factors-inhibiting-entrepreneurial-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Religion – religious believes may deter entrepreneurial investments in items such as night clubs and pubs.
b) Language – establishing businesses in areas where language barrier may allow poor communication or fear of invasion.
c) Personal relationship – Married people may avoid getting involved in business activities since no time is spared for the family.
d) Attitude towards innovation</p>
<ul>
<li>Especially in cultures which oppose innovation due to fear of change
e) Networks – poor networking and ability to meet people limit new</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="means-of-generating-a-business-idea">Means of Generating a Business Idea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#means-of-generating-a-business-idea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) identifying a need
b) brainstorming
c) building on ones skill, hobbies or interests

<p>Listening to what People say.</p>
<ul>

<li>Attribute listening</li>
<li>This method of generating business ideas is based on changing the way one looks at something in order to find a new use for it.</li>
<li>It attempts to answer the question – what do we do with this product.</li>
</ul>
<p>Gaining from Waste</p>
<ul>
<li>What would appear waste can be used – say recycles to create a new opportunity. Others</li>
<li>By soliciting ideas by interview, reading, observations, listening</li>

<p>The Process of Screening a Business Idea.</p>
<ul>
<li>After generating business ideas – it is important that some evaluation through a screening process be made.</li>
<li>The screening process is a systematic evaluation ideas in order to select the best idea which would suit one.</li>
<li>The screening process must be done carefully, objectively, soberly and without any emotions.</li>
<li>The business idea screening is required even when there is only one idea to consider. This is because this is a stage of starting a business that may be not be profitable or may be difficult to run</li>
<li>The screening process must therefore evaluate the following</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Personal Evaluation</p>
<ul>
<li>the objective for going to business</li>
<li>personal interests</li>
<li>The degree of commitment to the business or others e.g. family.</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Personal Skills</p>
<ul>
<li>The self SWOT analysis – this aims at analyzing ones</li>
</ul>
<p>a. Strengths
b. Weaknesses
c. Opportunities
d. Treats</p>
<ul>
<li>“Strengths” and “Weaknesses” should focus on the internal environment (management, product/service), whilst “Opportunities” and “Threats” should focus on the external environment (economy, market and competitors).</li>
<li>Clearly, it is important that your business idea has significant strengths (or can develop them) and a plan to counter to any weaknesses. Your business idea should be developed to take advantage of any opportunities and thought should be given to how you would respond to threats.</li>
<li>A SWOT analysis should provide proof to you, your investors and funders etc., of the likelihood of your business succeeding or failing. If your analysis suggests it will fail you need to reconsider your idea.</li>
</ul>
<p>The screening process or evaluation helps identify;</p>
<ul>
<li>Strengths: E.g. Distinctive competence, Adequate finances, Access to economies of scale, Good innovation ability, proven management</li>
</ul>
<p>Page 21 of 165
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Weakness: E.g. Lack of key skill, Internal operations problems, Low morale, Poor track records, Weak internal image
Opportunities: E.g. Potential customers, Potential goodwill, A favorable social environment
Threats: Strong competitions, Adverse government policies, Political instability, mismanaged economy, Unfavorable legislation</p>
<p>d) Market evaluations</p>
<ul>
<li>The aim is to create assurance of adequate market</li>
<li>The main components include</li>
<li>i.) Consumer demand analysis</li>
<li>ii.) Product price and placements</li>
<li>iii.) No. of competitors in markets.</li>
</ul>
<p>e) An analysis of availability of raw materials in terms of</p>
<ul>
<li>i) Adequacy</li>
<li>ii) Reliability</li>
<li>iii) Price</li>
</ul>
<p>f) Analysis of providing technology in terms of</p>
<ul>
<li>i) Appropriateness</li>
<li>ii) Affordability</li>
</ul>
<p>g) An analysis of skills available
h) Analysis of the government policies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-a-good-business-idea">Characteristics of a Good Business idea.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-a-good-business-idea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Easy to manage and involve minimal risk.</li>
<li>Does not require excessive capital investments</li>
<li>Offers a good returns on capital</li>
<li>The idea has scope for growth, expansion and diversification</li>
<li>Comparative with owner's goal and interest</li>
<li>Not against expectation of the society</li>
<li>Has a short gestation period</li>
<li>Has a readily available market</li>
<li>Easy to exit when necessary.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-sources-of-new-ideas">The sources of new ideas<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-sources-of-new-ideas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Some of the more frequently used sources of business ideas for entrepreneurs include.</li>
<li>Consumers</li>
<li>Potential entrepreneurs not only pay attention to potential customers but also monitor their potential needs through allowing the customers to express their opinions.</li>
<li>Existing products and services</li>
<li>Through monitoring and evaluating competitive products and services.</li>
<li>Distribution channels</li>
<li>Contact with members of the distribution channels since they are familiar with the needs of the market and give suggestions of new products and consumer needs.</li>
<li>Government</li>
<li>Can be a source of a business idea through</li>
<li>a) The patent office which contains numerous product possibilities.</li>
<li>b) Official government magazines</li>
<li>c) Government regulatory bodies e.g KBS</li>
<li>d) Government shows and exhibitions</li>
<li>Research and development</li>
<li>a. Is the largest source of new ideas to the entrepreneur.</li>
<li>Education – i.e. picking a given line of study e.g. construction, Vocational training programmes and experience.</li>
</ul>
