<p>vii.) Personal hobbies especially for craft entrepreneurs.
viii.) Personal contacts and observations through.
Interactions, Newspapers and magazines.
ix.) Conducting surveys and interviews of the people around.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition-of-a-business-opportunity">Definition of a Business Opportunity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-a-business-opportunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ A business opportunity may be defined as an attractive project idea. Which an entrepreneur accepts for investment on the basis of what is known about the possible success for the project.
☑ A real business opportunity can be distinguished from a mere possibility through the following two ingredients.</p>
<p>i. A good market scope
ii. An attractive return on investment (profit) Qualities</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-a-good-business-opportunity">(Characteristics) of a Good Business Opportunity:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-a-good-business-opportunity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are qualities of a good business opportunity.</p>
<p>a. Demand – there should exist a good market scope
b. Returns on investment – i.e. the business should be sufficiently profitable.
c. Availability of raw materials
d. Enough skilled people.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="evaluation-of-business-opportunities-objectives-of-a-pre-feasibility-study">Evaluation of Business Opportunities (objectives of a pre-feasibility study)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#evaluation-of-business-opportunities-objectives-of-a-pre-feasibility-study" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Once a business opportunity has been identified, one needs to confirm that it is viable through a pre-feasibility study.
☑ The main objective of a feasibility study is to determine whether.</p>
<p>a. the investment opportunity is promising enough
b. The project is viable from the marketing manufacturing and other points of view.</p>
<p>c. Any aspect of the project that may be crucial to call for in-depth analysis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-purpose-of-pre-feasibility-study-market-research">The Purpose of Pre-feasibility Study (Market Research)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-purpose-of-pre-feasibility-study-market-research" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i.) To verify that the investment opportunity is promising enough to make a firm decision.
ii.) To confirm that the project is viable from the</p>
<p>a. Marketing
b. Manufacturing and
c. Other points of view</p>
<p>iii.) To identify any aspects of the project that is critical or crucial enough to call for in-depth analysis.</p>
<p>iv.) To acquire comprehensive technical, economic and commercial data for the final investment decision.
v.) To enable an in-depth study of aspects such as</p>
<p>Market potential, Technical requirements, Managerial ability, financial projections and analysis, Risks evaluation, Business environmental analysis.</p>
<p>vi.) To enable sourcing reliable information such as</p>
<p>a. Authorized publications
b. Consultant’s openings.</p>
<p>vii.) To establish the final outcome of whether or not to proceed with the business.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="business-incubation">Business Incubation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#business-incubation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Business incubation is the process of nurturing small and start-up initiatives or business to relative maturity to become self-sustaining business, healthy and wealth-generating entities.
☑ The failure rate of any start-up business stands at 90% globally.
☑ The main causes of business failure;</p>
<p>Page 23 of 165
This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>i) Insufficient capital for start-up. ii) Insufficient knowledge of business and industry. iii) Lack of Entrepreneurial and business skills. iv) Lack of Managerial skills. v) Inadequate Training. vi) Lack of credit facilities. vii) Lack of markets. viii) Insufficient knowledge of markets. Inadequate infrastructure.</p>
<p>ii) Non-Empowering political environment.</p>
<p>☑ For these reasons, many businesses which are ill-equipped do not survive. A business incubator is important for precisely those reasons above to provide these support services.</p>
<p>☑ Statistics show that the success rate for incubated businesses initiatives is very high (over 80%) are bound to succeed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-incubation-process">The Incubation Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-incubation-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ The business incubation programmes are designed to accelerate successful development of entrepreneurial companies through a vary of support resources and services.</p>
<p>☑ Incubators vary in the way they deliver their services in their organizational structure and in the types of clients they serve.</p>
<p>☑ Business incubators differ from research and technology in their dedication to start-up and early stage businesses.</p>
<p>☑ Research and Technology institutes tend to be large scale projects that house everything from corporate government or university labs to very small companies.</p>
<p>☑ The research institutions do not offer business assistance services which are the main objective of business incubation.</p>
<p>☑ Unlike many business assistance programmes business incubators do not serve any and all companies.</p>
<p>☑ Entrepreneurs who may wish to enter a business incubation program must apply for admission.</p>
<p>☑ Acceptance criteria vary from program to program but in general only those with feasible business ideas and workable business plan are admitted.</p>
<p>☑ The time a company spends in an incubation programme vary widely depending on a number of factors, including the type of business and the Entrepreneur’s level of business Expertise.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-benefits-of-incubation">The Benefits of Incubation.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-benefits-of-incubation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Creating jobs and wealth</p>
<p>☑ Fosters a community’s Entrepreneurial climate - Technology commercialization.</p>
<p>☑ Diversification of Local Resource.</p>
<p>☑ Acceleration of local development.</p>
<p>☑ Facilitation of Business creation and growth.</p>
<p>☑ Encouraging entrepreneurship especially women.</p>
<p>☑ Revitalization of the community as a whole.</p>
<p>☑ Growth of Private Sector Investment.</p>
<p>☑ Increased Tax Revenue.</p>
<p>☑ Equitable Development.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="protections-of-business-ideas-maintaining-secrecy">Protections of Business ideas &amp; maintaining Secrecy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protections-of-business-ideas-maintaining-secrecy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Most entrepreneurs will not be inventors, at least not in the classic sense but all entrepreneurs are concerned with protecting their business ideas, especially when those ideas are related to; oUn usual production oUnique designs et.c
☑ And for this to be done understand the “patent law” becomes but simply paramount
☑ When entrepreneurs want to protect unusual brand name, products business ideas or simply establishing ownership, then understanding trademarks and copyrights if vital as a way of protecting a business idea.
☑ The government law pertaining to; o Patents o Trademarks o Copyrights – are not complicated
☑ Many entrepreneurs file their own patent claims or prepare documentation for trademark or copyright protection without professional help from the Attorney or patent agents.
☑ However it is always wise to have professional assistance though the laws are simple. Ways of Protecting Business ideas a) A patent
☑ A patent is a grant of property right by the government to an inventor. It is issued thought the commissioner of patent rights, and the most common type of patent is called a utility patent. All patent however, have the distinction of being assets with a commercial value because they provide exclusive rights of ownership the patent holders.
☑ Patents are exclusive property rights that can be sold, transferred, or used as collateral much alike other valuable assets.
☑ The patent law stipulates broad categories of what can and cannot be patented and in the words of the statute any person who “invents or discovers any new and useful process, machine manufacture, or composition of matter, or ay new and useful improvements thereof may obtain a patent”
☑ Anything that is patentable must be new and useful ( must have some demonstrated function) Trademarks
☑ Trademarks include any word, name, symbol or distinguishing device or any combination thereof adopted and used by a manufacturer or merchant to identify his goods and distinguish them from those manufactured or sold by others.
☑ Trade-marks can be names used in commerce such as KCA it can be a symbol or any distinguishing device artistic in nature.
An important qualification for a trademark is that mark, name etc. must be used commercially.</p>
<p>Service mark Is similar to a trademark and can be registered in the same way with the sale protection A service market can be a name, wording used in advertising symbols or artistic figures that create a distinctive service concept.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-4-10-copyrights">2.4.10 Copyrights<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-4-10-copyrights" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Are similar to patents in establishing ownership and protection for creative ideas but they pertain to the intellectual property.
☑ The copyright is distinct from patents and trademarks in that intellectual property is protected for the life of the originator plus a further 50 years.
☑ This protection affords an extraordinary property right and substantial estates. It extends protection to author, composers and artists.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-4-12-trade-secrets">2.4.12 Trade Secrets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-4-12-trade-secrets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☐ Are proprietary information used in the course of business to gain an advantage in manufacturing or commercialization of products or services. ☑ Trade secrets i)formulas ii)patterns iii)list of customers iv)data bases v)chemical compounds vi)combinations of ingredients for commercial products vii)process of manufacturing viii)Complied information.</p>
<p>☐ Every organization must keep their secrets because oModern communications systems contain so much information which if not guarded, the business may collapse. o Employees leaving may disseminate information to competitors. o In any business to maintain a market Niche, then desire to protect their product.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-4-13-trade-secrets">2.4.13 Trade Secrets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-4-13-trade-secrets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In certain instances the entrepreneur may prefer to maintain an idea or process as confidential, and eventually sell or license it as a trade secret.</p>
<p>☑ The trade secret will have a life as long as the idea or process remains secret.
☑ A trade secret in not covered by any law but is recognized under a governing body.
☑ Employees involved in working with an idea or process may be asked to first sign a confidential information agreement that will protect against their giving out the trade secret either while as employees or when leaving the organization – this is called trade secret non-disclosure agreement.
☑ Most entrepreneurs have limited resources so they choose not to find means of protecting their ideas or products or services.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-4-15-licensing">2.4.15 Licensing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-4-15-licensing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Licensing may be defined as an agreement between two parties, where one party has proprietary rights over some information, process or technology protected by a patent, trademark or copyright.
☑ This arrangement specified in a contract requires the licence to pay royalty or some other specified sum to the holder of the proprietary rights in return for permission to copy the patent trade mark or copyright.
☑ Licensing has significance as a marketing strategy to holders of patents, trademarks or copyrights to grow their business in a new market when they lack resources or experiences in such markets.
It is also an important marketing strategy for entrepreneurs who wish to start a new venture but need permission to a copy or incorporate the patent trademark or copyright with the ideas.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-5-product-safety-and-liability">2.5 Product Safety and Liability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-5-product-safety-and-liability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is very important for the entrepreneur to assess whether any product that is to be marketed in the new venture is subject to any regulations under the consumer product.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> In addition to setting standards for products the commission also has a great deal of responsibility and power to identify what to consider being a substantial hazard and barring any products that may be considered unsafe.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="entrepreneurial-motivation">ENTREPRENEURIAL MOTIVATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entrepreneurial-motivation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Entrepreneur motivation is the drives, the desires, the need to achieve or fulfil certain entrepreneurial needs.</li>
<li>Motivation is that which causes you to behave in the way you behave i.e. the why of behavior</li>
<li>Entrepreneurial motivation are those factors and forces or events that energizes an individual, his desires and the needs to go into and sustain a business venture.</li>
<li>Types of motivation;
a) Internal Motivation Factors
b) External Motivation Factors</li>
<li>Internal Motivations and Drives
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Refers to those personal traits and desires that induce a person to become an entrepreneur. Such motivations are;
i. Employment Creation Need.
ii. Need for independence or self-Reliance: one may want to be one's own boss especially if one doesn't like taking orders from others. You may also want to be in control of your own destiny (internal locus of control) making your own business decisions, using your time maximally.
iii. Need for Power: Need to exercise power over others and need to control others. People with a high need for power have a greater concern for exercising influence and control.
iv. Need for Recognition: We normally strive to get recognition about our achievement in life, by our peers, family and society. If you aspire to be recognized, then this could be an important drive for you to go into selfemployment
v. Need for Security: All men thrive to be free from anxiety;
☐ Anxiety about our very survival
☐ Survival of our near dearest
☐ Anxiety about the future, both for ourselves as well as for our families
It is for this reason that we all strive to maximize our returns, wage employment may not meet this anxiety especially if we are not pensionable.
vi. Self-actualization need;
Refers to the need to accomplish that which you as a person is capable of achieving, the need to be unique. Through entrepreneurial activities and with dedication and commitment, you can realize this need, a need that is</li>
</ul>
<p>Page 27 of 165
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>very difficult to realize by all or most individuals in the formal employment.</p>
<ul>
<li>External Motivations and Drives</li>
<li>☑ Unlike internal motivations which are in your inner being, the external motivations refer to those that are provided by others, especially the legal authorities and society in general.</li>
<li>☑ These provide an enabling environment for entrepreneurship. Some of them are;</li>
<li>i. Infrastructure: To operate efficiently, any business requires the provision of certain basic facilities such as power, water, electricity, communication and accessibility.</li>
<li>ii. Credit Facilities: Refers to provision of money through loans to be used in starting as well as expanding a business. It is usually very rare for a person to have adequate finance to start or expand his own business. Some of the external sources include;</li>
<li>☐ Government agencies</li>
<li>☐ Banks and non-bank financial institutions</li>
<li>☐ Non-governmental organizations</li>
<li>iii. Information Support</li>
</ul>
<p>Entrepreneurs need information related to the market for their products since they may not have resources to carryout significant marketing research, yet the success of business depends on how well they understand the market. It is therefore necessary for such information to be made easily accessible to entrepreneurs.</p>
<p>iv. Pricing Policy</p>
<p>Pricing policy of the government should be an incentive to an entrepreneur. It should motivate more and more people to venture into such entrepreneurial activities. When venturing into a particular business, you will first have to understand the pricing policy applied in such an industry and assess how that policy will affect your earnings and the survival of your business.</p>
<p>v. Tax Policy</p>
<p>It is important that the tax policy act as a motivator to entrepreneurship, all too often, the authorities in their endeavor to raise revenue resort to increasing indirect taxes such as value added tax and customs duty.</p>
<p>vi. Legal Control</p>
<p>Legal controls and the attendant bureaucracy should be minimized as much as possible so as to attract entrepreneurs. The legal control can be manifested in the licensing requirements for establishing various types of businesses.</p>
<p>vii. Political Climate</p>
<p>The prevailing political climate should be conducive to smooth operation of business. This climate should be that there is no discrimination and conducive law and order, no tribal barrier.</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>viii. Technical Technology Assistance</p>
<p>This covers giving advice on production aspects of the business and the projection studies for lending institutions.</p>
<p>ix. Training Consultancy Assistance</p>
<p>The government offers vocational training courses for entrepreneurs. It also provides counseling to help entrepreneurs solve their problems. Eg of government agencies is Kenya Institute of Business Training (KIBT)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maslow-s-need-theory">Maslow's Need Theory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maslow-s-need-theory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Theory of human needs is identified with the psychologist Abraham Maslow. This theory is based on three specific assumptions:</p>
<ol>
<li>That human beings are never satisfied. Their wants are determined by what they have. When people are hungry or thirsty, the quest for food or water influences how they behave. However if food and water is acquired, the same person will want something else, perhaps a safe place to live in or a social status.</li>
<li>A satisfied need does not cause behavior. Once people satisfy their need for safety, they are motivated by yet unsatisfied needs, not the ones – that are satisfied,</li>
<li>Human needs are arranged in hierarchy of importance. These needs range from low level biological (physiological) needs to such high level needs as self-actualization.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Physiological Needs:</strong> The need for Food, Clothing Shelter. They are required for survival. We require money to satisfy these basic needs. If we do not have any source of income and cannot get wage employment, we may be motivated to entrepreneurship.</p>
<p><strong>Safety or security needs:</strong> Once or basic needs are satisfied, our behavior is no longer motivated by them. At this point we begin to worry about the security or safety of our families ie the need to be free from physical danger and fear of loss of job. For entrepreneurs, since their ability to</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-e359529c.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>Page 29 of 165</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>cater for these needs depend on how hard they work, these needs will motivate their behavior. They save money to use in the case of illness, purchase of insurance policies.</p>
<p><strong>Belongingness Need (Affiliation or acceptance needs):</strong> Once safety needs are satisfied, they no longer motivate us to work harder. Since we are social beings, we need to belong, to be accepted by others like family, work groups, mentors.</p>
<p><strong>Esteem needs:</strong> They are more abstract than physiological, safety and belonging needs. This kind of needs produces such satisfaction as; Power, Prestige, Status, self-confidence.</p>
<p><strong>Self-Actualization Needs:</strong> Means making the most of what we have to maximize our potential. They want to achieve the best and believe that no one is better than them. They aspire for a standard of excellence.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-demotivate-people-to-entrepreneurship">What demotivate people to Entrepreneurship?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-demotivate-people-to-entrepreneurship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Lack of proper information</li>
<li>Fear of competition. Fear of taking risk</li>
<li>Inhibiting government laws</li>
<li>Lack of adequate start-up capital</li>
<li>Lack of knowledge and skills</li>
<li>Wrong attitudes towards employment</li>
</ul>
<p>State how Maslow’s Hierarchy of needs theory is relate to Motivation in entrepreneurship.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="entrepreneurial-competencies">ENTREPRENEURIAL COMPETENCIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entrepreneurial-competencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="leadership">LEADERSHIP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Leadership is the ability to inspire, influence, persuade others to give maximum effort and cooperation willingly and voluntarily towards the attainment of the unplanned goals.</li>
<li>Good leadership is a necessity in any business organization. It is important your portray appropriate leadership qualities such as leadership behavior, leading and motivating others, leadership responsibilities, leaders influence and activities;</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="leadership-behavior">Leadership Behavior<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#leadership-behavior" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>As a leader, your should have the following qualities:</li>
</ul>
<p>a) Vision and foresight: you should look into the future when making plans, you need vision in order to be able to determine how you want your business to develop</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>b) Strong desire to influence others: You can influence your staff if they have confidence and trust in you.</p>
<p>c) Ability to learn from past errors and build on past experience ie experience is the best teacher, you should be able to improve your business through learning from experience and avoiding past mistakes</p>
<p>d) High ambition: Should always aim high and for the best in your undertakings and expectations.</p>
<p>e) Imagination: as a leader you should see beyond the horizon</p>
<p>f) Creativity: You should be as original as possible in ideas and activities. You should have the daring to try new methods of operation.</p>
<p>g) Initiative as a leader, you have the role of getting things started. You should also find new and better ways of doing things you are the agent of change.</p>
<p>h) Good human relations: as a leader you should sell good image of your business.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="leading-and-motivating-others">Leading and Motivating Others<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#leading-and-motivating-others" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As an entrepreneur success depends on how you motivate your employees. The following techniques should be employed:</p>
<p>i. Built Workers self-esteem- By praising the good work done by your employees, you are building confidence in selves. Appreciate what they have done.</p>
<p>ii. Inform employees- Tell your staff what you are trying to accomplish.</p>
<p>iii. Delegation of authority and responsibility:- Good delegation will allow you as a leader to devote more time to important and crucial issues within your business.</p>
<p>iv. Maintain contact: know your staff well enough by maintaining personal contact.</p>
<p>v. Apply reinforcement principal:- you should reward behaviours that you consider desirable because people tend to repeat rewarded behavior. Don't reward undesirable behavior as people tend not to repeat unrewarded behavior.</p>
<p>vi. Be an active listener: By active listening you will be an effective communicator which is an important quality of a leader. Your employees will take it that you appreciate them and have concern in them.</p>
<p>vii. Set specific goals: set specific clearly understood measurable goals and continuously review them.</p>
<p>viii. Take collective action- When you must deal with some negative aspects of a workers performance you should talk to that worker in private, never criticize a worker in public.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="leadership-styles">Leadership Styles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#leadership-styles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Leadership styles are divided into three classification;</p>
<p>a) Autocratic Style:</p>
<ul>
<li>The oldest and most traditional form of leadership style. In this style, the manager draws a very firm discipline line.</li>
</ul>
<p>Page 31 of 165</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>○ Everybody knows what he/she can or cannot do. Many like this form of leadership because it gives a sense of purpose and security.
They know what is expected of them and they know that they must leave up to certain standards</p>
<p>b) Laissez Faire / Free-Reign A very permissive type of style, employees are left alone to reach their own potential.
○ Some people are responsive to these style and do not abuse their freedom, others take advantage of the climate and do not leave up to their potential.</p>
<p>c) Democratic Style This style depends upon the organization, its objectives and the personalities of its people.
In democratic climate a manager builds a sense of union and common interest among his/her workers.
It is at times even hard to recognize who the manager is.
○ Leaders set discipline lines against which nobody seems to object.</p>
<p>Most leaders use a combination of styles, depending on the group and the situations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="theory-x-and-theory-y">Theory X and Theory Y<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theory-x-and-theory-y" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ According to Mc Gregory each manager will manage his employees according to his own attitudes and ideas about people, their needs and their motivations.
If an appointed a manager believes that individuals are naturally lazy, then he or she will treat subordinate employees in a certain way, such as issuing precise orders and exercising tight control over their work.
For purposes of comparison he stated that the extremes in contrasting attitudes among managers could be classified as Theory X and Theory Y</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Theory X</th><th>Theory Y</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1.Inert, lazy, prodded</td><td>Naturally active, striving</td></tr><tr><td>2.Work for threat of hunger, loss of job</td><td>Work to achieve goals, find satisfaction, build good life</td></tr><tr><td>3.Pay is almost the only motive</td><td>Many motives, achievement, recognition, service</td></tr><tr><td>4.Dependent, must be directed, push, needs leader to inspire</td><td>Independent capable of self-directing, setting own goal</td></tr><tr><td>5.Irresponsible, immature, must be closely supervised and carefully checked</td><td>Mature, responsible, capable of self-correction</td></tr><tr><td>6.Conformists-needs prescribed routine and resist change</td><td>Inventive, adaptive, creative needs to device new ways</td></tr><tr><td>7.Satisfied with good pay</td><td>Seeks broader meaning in work life</td></tr><tr><td>8.Not to be trusted</td><td>Usually trusted</td></tr></tbody></table>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sources-of-influence-in-leadership">Sources of influence in Leadership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-influence-in-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Legitimate Authority: - A person may gain compliance from sub-ordinates because of the authority which is associated with the office the person holds. The power of the office is often derived from the person’s responsibilities as a manager, administrator or politician. Owners of business enterprises enjoy the power to reward, reprimand or punish their subordinates.</p>
<p>b) Economic Power: - the clout that comes with economic might sometimes referred to as reward power. So a person who is in a position to administer economic rewards, could influence the behavior of subordinates through appointments or denial of such rewards.</p>
<p>c) Coercive Power: a person who is in a position to get other people to do things by the use of force or threats and intimidation is said to possess coercive involuntary action where the subordinates submit their consent only because they fear the repercussions of punishment or violence.</p>
<p>d) Persuasion; There are times when persons in positions of responsibility need to use wit and sweet words in order to get things done through others.</p>
<p>e) Referent power: Is based on the subordinate’s identification with the leader. The leader exercises influence because of perceived attractiveness, personal character, reputation or what is called “charisma”. E.g. doctors, athletes, academicians, wealthy people. This respect could be turned into a source of influence for those who admire a particular person.</p>
<p>f) Expert Power.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="theories-of-leadership">Theories of Leadership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#theories-of-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Trait Theory</p>
<p>☑ Assumes that leaders are born not made.</p>
<p>☑ Leadership consists of certain inherited characteristics or personality traits which distinguish leaders from followers. E.g. need for achievement, focus, assertiveness, etc b) Situational Theory</p>
<p>☑ Leadership is considered to be a function of the situation which a leader emerges and works. It is based on assumption that leadership is basically situational.</p>
<p>☑ The person who becomes the leader of the work group is thought to be the person who knows best what to do and seen by the group as the most suitable leader in the particular situation</p>
<p>c) Behavioral Theory</p>
<p>☑ It is based on the assumption that leadership effectiveness depends upon what the leader does. The leadership behavior is the product of the leader and the followers.</p>
<p>☑ A leader uses his skills to exercise influence and modify behavior of his subordinates. Qualities of a leader: Should have energy, perseverance, education-up-to-date, intelligent, personality, creative, innovative, optimistic, balanced, objective, enthusiastic</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="decision-making">DECISION MAKING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#decision-making" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ This is selection from among alternatives of a course of action.
☑ Is a process of choosing from among various alternatives?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="categories-of-business-problems">Categories of business problems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#categories-of-business-problems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Inadequacy of resources such as raw materials to produce products, skilled manpower, capital etc.
ii. Organizational problems such as poor delegation of duties, undefined rules etc
iii. Environmental problems such as poor business locations, poor or unsafe working conditions etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-to-identify-a-problem-in-a-business">How to identify a problem in a business.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-identify-a-problem-in-a-business" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Past Experience: where you have experienced a similar problem ii. Conducting a survey to find out if activities are carried out according to plan
iii. Hiring consultancy services
iv. Employing work study methods</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-decision-making">Methods of Decision Making<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-decision-making" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are several methods you can use to make business decisions, among them we have;</p>
<p>i. Rule of Thumb: A decision is made based on existing established procedures e.g. based on laws, customs, religion, etc. You can't change
ii. Committee Approach/ Team work: It's where using a selected number of people from the main group to make a decision which will be accepted by all.
iii. Critical Path Analysis: This is making decision stage by stage until the final decision is reached.
iv. Brainstorming: This is where all members of a group develop ideas for a solution
v. Problem solving Chart
vi. Solution Evaluation Form</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="steps-of-the-decision-making-process">Steps of the Decision Making process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#steps-of-the-decision-making-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Identify the major problem e.g. low productivity</li>
<li>Determine major causes of the problem e.g. low salaries, poor working conditions</li>
<li>Determine potential solutions – how to solve</li>
<li>Evaluate potential solutions</li>
<li>Select the best solution 6) Implement the solution 7) Verify the solution. <strong>Problem Solving Chart</strong></li>
</ol>
<p>☑ You can use a problem solving chart as one way of organizing possible solutions to the problems.
☑ After completing it you will be able to analyze alternative solutions in terms of potential advantages, disadvantages and consequences. A space is provided on the chart for four possible solutions.</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ If there are more than four possible solutions, it may be difficult for you to analyze the information adequately.
✓ Listing potential advantage will indicate how each potential disadvantage will illustrate how the potential solution will adversely affect you
✓ In some instances, an advantage or disadvantage may be the same for two or more alternative solutions.
✓ Potential consequences you identify in the last column will be the results of analyzing the potential advantages and disadvantages.
✓ They should equal the potential net result of implementing a particular solution.
✓ The problem solving chart can help you to analyse and solve major problems which would otherwise have an adverse effect on your business.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Alternative Solution</th><th>Potential Advantage</th><th>Potential Disadvantage</th><th>Potential consequences</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1. <div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="solution-evaluation-form">Solution Evaluation Form<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#solution-evaluation-form" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Another procedure for analyzing potential solutions is to identify reasons for and reasons against each potential solution.
To use the solution evaluation form to the best advantage, you should: 1. Write a brief description of the problem at the top of the form</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Write a brief description of the proposed solution.</li>
<li>In the reasons for column, list important factors which would favour implementing the proposed solution.</li>
<li>In the reasons against column list important factors for not implementing the proposed solutions.</li>
<li>Rate each factor by its importance to you. The numerical ratings might be 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 where a low rating of 1 indicates that the factor affects the problem only slightly and a high rating of 5 indicates that the factor is extremely important in making your decision. Each factor in the reason for column and each factor in the reason against column would receive a numerical rating</li>
<li>Add the ratings in each of the two rating columns, the column with a higher total will give you some indication of the potential for a particular solution. If there is a big difference between the two totals (in favor of reasons for the solution) you may feel more secure in the use of this technique to make a decision. If there is little difference in totals for both columns, it might indicate that you need additional information about the problem.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-use-of-group-participation">The Use of Group Participation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-use-of-group-participation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Are Many advantages of involving the members of a workgroup in a decision
☑ Some positive aspects of group decision making are;</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>The sum total of the groups knowledge is greater</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The group generally develops a much wider range of alternatives in the decision process.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Participation increases the acceptability of the decision to the group</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Group members better understand why a decision was made ☑ Negative aspects of group decisions:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It takes more time</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>One individual may dominate and control the group</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Social pressures to confirm may inhibit group members</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Competition can become overly intense among the group members</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Groups have a tendency to accept the first potentially positive alternative</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The decision is often a compromise that is likely to be unsatisfactory</p>
</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="time-management">TIME MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#time-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Time is a measure of life.
☑ A unique resource, shared equally, cannot be stored, cannot be replaced once it is lost.
☑ Time is an entrepreneurs' scarcest resource &amp; unless it's managed, nothing else can be managed
☑ Time Management is the management of the activities we engage in during our time to achieve a goal.
☑ Some of the factors that contribute to time wasting in a business include;</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>i. Failure to delegate duties:- an entrepreneur should not do all the work by him / herself but delegate it to others.
ii. Poor mailing process:- This is where a mail is taken to a wrong person who might hold it, therefore urgent matter might not be attended to.
iii. Unnecessary interruptions by friends or relatives iv. Poorly conducted meetings, whereby people talk much and not sensible matters
v. Poor scheduling of events- avoid postponing of activities when they are supposed to be attended to.
vi. Excessive paper work. Indecisiveness- unable to decide ☑ To avoid this pitfalls, you should do the following:</p>
<p>i. Keep a business dairy ii. Select your priorities, whether to attend a wedding or attend to your customers iii. Avoid unnecessary interruptions i.e. meeting your relatives and friends iv. Reduce paperwork, by delegating some to your subordinates/ support staff or introducing ICT facilities.</p>
<p>v. Avoid postponing activities – do them when they are required vi. Keep to schedule- do activities according to the way you have arranged them, don't change</p>
<p>vii. Keep clearing your desks in-trays- have a clean and organized working place viii. Be time conscious and use time carefully.</p>
<p>☑ To Manage your Time</p>
<p>☐ Draw – up and action plan – ie “things to do list”
☐ Set out priorities based on what is urgent and important
☐ Schedule your time realistically
☐ Delegate as much as you can and monitor progress realized.
☐ Attempt to perform as much/many tasks as possible during the early part of the day. “use 20% of your time to accomplish 50% of task”
☐ Let workers work within their limits
☐ If any new tasks arises during the working time, advert the risks and allocate the priority rate and control interruption. Always try to allow time during the day and keep in touch with your workers. Allow time to think about tomorrow.
☐ Try to have competent personnel – skilled personnel. Improve your communication skills.</p>
<p>Tools of Time Management: Time tables, Schedules, Programmes</p>
<p>Question: What are the benefits of effective time management in your business?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="change">CHANGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Change is the need to make or become different, to replace or improve, to reform or reorganize to fit to the current situation which results in higher productivity or performance. ☑ Is a systematic planned effort to improve effectiveness of the business. Change is risky, uncertain ☑ As an entrepreneur you play a key role of managing change in your business.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="need-for-change">Need for Change<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#need-for-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) There is need to adopt / adapt
b) To remain viable (economically)
c) We want growth (sales + profit), employees, customers (increase market share), diversify
d) Enhance chances of survival (Change before Change changes you).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="reasons-for-change">Reasons for change<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reasons-for-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) People change because they are dissatisfied with the status quo.
b) Interdepartmental conflicts – conflicts in departments
c) The need to cut costs
d) To need to improve efficiency
e) Need for company or personal security
f) Existence of a new demand in the market
g) Tough international and national competition
h) Change in technology etc</p>
<p>These conditions create threats and present opportunities in an organization</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-that-influence-change-in-your-business">Factors that influence change in your business<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-that-influence-change-in-your-business" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Economic activities: e.g. changes in the prices of some input
b) Competition: The competitors activities; be watchful on competition to respond in good time e.g. by aggressive advertising, reducing the price
c) The government and political environment: New policies, regulations relating to taxation and remuneration policies
d) Technology: For adaptability and business growth. Go for the new technology
e) Educational and social factors: e.g your customers changes in education status, taste, family size, status, age, sex, population distribution,</p>
<p>The above call for change in terms of quality, price, promptness in delivery, packaging, labelling of your product etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-change">Types of change:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Change of Product: e.g you change your products labelling, size, packaging, color, taste, quality, smell
b) Change of service: change in terms of promptness (quick/fastness) and quality service
c) Change of technology: e.g. Tools and equipment, material, technical skills, procedures, production methods
d) Change of policy.: Change of objectives, goals and policies to follow to meet government policies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="why-people-resist-change">Why People Resist Change<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-people-resist-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Fear of the unknown (don't know what next)</li>
<li>Misinformation (false information), no information at all, no communication</li>
</ol>
<p>Page 38 of 165</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Threat to status quo</li>
<li>Threat to power base – Most want to retain their normal ways of life. Fear of no one recognizing business in foreign places, location/town</li>
<li>Miss-trust or distrust of change agents. Eg some people don't take change because of the people who bring about or initiate that particular change.</li>
<li>Fear of possible failure:- either social or economic failures</li>
<li>No perceived tangible benefits – people want immediate returns / gains</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="managing-change">Managing Change<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#managing-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>5 basic steps in the process of change management / implementation</p>
<ol>
<li>Precise definition of the operational changes needed</li>
<li>Define how the new working methods will affect particular people and groups</li>
<li>Identification of attitudes and perspectives currently held by employees and how this support current practice</li>
<li>Outline statement of attitudes and perspectives necessary to enable people too adapt successfully to new environments and new working methods</li>
<li>Implementation of measure designed to change existing attitudes.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="coping-with-competition">COPING WITH COMPETITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#coping-with-competition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Competition is the act to vie for customers or market.</p>
<p><strong>Direct competitors</strong> – Services / Products which are similar to the same already in the market.</p>
<p><strong>Indirect competitor</strong> – offering different kinds of goods/ services to the same market/customers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="identification">Identification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#identification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Identify and list out names, location and activities of all your competitors.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="analysis">Analysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#analysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You analyze yourself and your competitors on the basis of yourself and your competitors non the basis of:</p>
<p>a. Market: What is your/ the market? What share of the market do you/they have? What advantages do you/they have in servicing your/their market segments?
b. Product: How does your product quality compare with the competitors? What special services do you / they offer? Do you/they have a programme to improve your/their products? Is there a possibility of developing a new/ or improved product to satisfy new needs?
c. Production: How do you compare your technology with the competitors? How do you compare sources of raw materials with those of your competitors? How do your skills (and those of your workers) compare with the competitors? What advantages / disadvantages does your / their location have?
d. Finance: How do you compare your financial resources with your competitors?
e. Government Policy: have you identified any opportunities or threats resulting from new or existing government policies(eg relaxation of import restrictions, introduction of VAT)</p>
<p>Page 39 of 165
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>f. Environment: Do changes in the general environment including the local communities offer any opportunities or threats to you for example there is a large number of young people whose tastes are different from the rest of society.</p>
<p>After obtaining answers to these and any other questions you develop arrange them in a strength/weaknesses / opportunities and threats SWOT Table.</p>
<p>Types of Competition</p>

Characterized by situation homogeneous (similar)
b) Oligopolistic competition
c) Monopolistic competition</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="entrepreneurial-skills">Entrepreneurial Skills<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#entrepreneurial-skills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

☑ An entrepreneur is someone who has good business idea and can turn that idea into reality. ☑ To be successful an entrepreneur must
☐ Identify an opportunity and understand it in great depth
