<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="market">MARKET<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#market" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="meaning-of-market">Meaning of Market:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meaning-of-market" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☐ A word derived from Latin; ‘Marcatus’ which means: Merchandise, trade or place where business is conducted.
☐ A place and where goods are bought and sold.
☐ Generally it means “anybody of persons who are in intimate business relations and carry on extensive transactions in any commodity.”
☐ A set of potential buyers and sellers of a product or service”</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-1-marketing-functions-and-strategies">3.1. Marketing Functions and strategies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-1-marketing-functions-and-strategies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Marketing consists of a multitude activities that include decisions about the company’s
☐ Products or services
☐ Pricing policies ☐ Promotions and
☐ Distribution methods.</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ The ultimate equal is to facilitate exchange between an enterprise and its customers.
✓ This exchange relationship exists as one party becomes willing to give something of value in order to receive something of value.
✓ Marketing is the process of conceiving than exchange and then accomplishing the tasks necessary to deliver the goods or services in a manner that satisfies customer and meets the business objective.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="marketing-functions">Marketing Functions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marketing-functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Marketing functions include:</p>
<p>i) The product – involves the planning, designing and developing the right type of the product in order to meet the customer’s satisfaction. It includes.
a) The packing of the product
b) The image
c) The brand name and label
d) The product
e) The product quality
f) The product range
g) The product output
h) The product warrantees and after sale services
i) The product policy</p>
<p>ii) The price – involves giving value which is charged by the suppliers. This is an important element of marking because;
a) It relates directly to the generation of revenue
b) Measures the profit cost and revenue elements.
c) Affects the product quality and quantity
d) Has a psychological impact on consumers. iii) The placement – also known as distribution is concerned with linking the seller and buyer through the product and involves elements of a) Inform potential customers
b) To convince and persuade existing customers to continuer choosing the product
c) To establish a business image or good will
d) To canter competition from other business dealings
e) To increase sales and revenue.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-marketing-strategy">The marketing strategy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-marketing-strategy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ This is a consciously formulated plan that describes how the new venture will compete.
✓ It focuses the business enterprise on a target market to fill the gap or create a niche.
✓ A well calculated marketing strategy provides guidelines for the entrepreneur concerning-:
☐ The expected results
☐ Allocation of resources ☐ Responsibilities for marketing
☐ Ways of controlling the enterprise.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-marketing-plan">The marketing Plan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-marketing-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Page 41 of 165
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Solidifies the marketing strategy by defining customers, sales forecasts and marketing objectives.</p>
<ul>
<li>It synthesizes market research and the entrepreneurs strategy into a blueprint for action</li>
<li>The plan is implemented through a marketing programme, which addresses the marketing activities decisions regarding product, the pricing, the promotional activities and the placement activities.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-marketing-mix">The Marketing Mix<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-marketing-mix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The term marketing mix refers to the apportionment of effort, combinations, designing and integration of all elements of marketing into a single programme aimed at achieving the objective of a business enterprise.</li>
<li>It is a detailed strategy, tasks, operations policies programmes, techniques and activities to which resources may be allocated to achieve marketing objectives.</li>
<li>The term is used to describe the combination of the four inputs which constitute a marketing system (4pcs) i.e. ☐ The product</li>
<li>☐ The price</li>
<li>☐ The placement</li>
<li>☐ The promotions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-4-ps-the-four-ps">The 4 Ps (the four Ps)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-4-ps-the-four-ps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The marketing mix denotes a combination of the various elements which in their totality make up a marketing system i.e. the product, the price, the placement and the promotion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-product">The Product<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-product" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The product element of the marketing mix involves the planning, designing and developing the right type of the product or service to meet the customer satisfaction. The main decisions involve: i) The product involve ii) The product size iii) The product quality iv) The product design v) The product range vi) The product volume vii) The product packaging viii) The brand name and label. ix) The product warranties and after sale service.</li>
<li>The product element of the marketing mix strives to establish. ☐ A product policy ☐ The product strategies ☐ The product mix</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-price">The Price<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-price" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pricing the product is an important element of the marketing mix.</li>
<li>Price is the value or sum of money which is charged by the supplier of a product or service from the buyer.</li>
<li>The financial price is the measurement of value and has the following importance.</li>
<li>i.) Economic value - because it relates to the generation of product revenue</li>
<li>ii.) Profits - through price profit cost and revenue elements are measurable. iii.) Product quality - price gives indication of the product quality.</li>
<li>iv.) The psychological element - price has a psychological influence in the market i.e high prices co-relate to superiority.</li>
<li>v.) Co-operate goals - are achievable through pricing decisions especially in formulating marking strategies</li>
<li>vi.) Meeting consumer expectations is measurable through price.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="placement">Placement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#placement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ Also known as distribution of goods physically
✓ This component of the marketing mix is concerned with linking the seller and the buyer.
✓ It involves the elements of - The channels of distribution - The transport means - The warehousing - The routing of the product.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="promotions">Promotions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#promotions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-promotional-message">(A promotional message)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-promotional-message" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ A product promotion is the act of providing information about a product to its prospective users in order to persuade them to buy, enjoy or choose the product
✓ Any product promotional message usually includes information which shows;</p>
<ul>
<li>That the product exists</li>
<li>That the product has ability to satisfy a particular want</li>
<li>The physical location where the product can be obtained or enjoyed ☐</li>
<li>The qualities that the product can be obtained or enjoyed.</li>
<li>The quantities that the product can be obtained ☐ the times when the product can be obtained ☐ The price of the product.</li>
</ul>
<p>✓ Exam quest, briefly explain what entails a promotional message.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="the-importance-of-product-promotion">The importance of product promotion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-importance-of-product-promotion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>i.) To inform potential customers about the existence qualities and other important details regarding a product.
ii.) To convince or persuade existing customers to continue buying the product and potential customers to choose it.
iii.) To establish a business image or goodwill among the existing and prospective customers
iv.) To facilitate more sales revenue.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="methods-of-product-promotion">Methods of Product Promotion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-product-promotion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ There are five main ways of promoting products namely; i) Advertising
ii) Personal selling
iii) Sales promotion
iv) Publicity
v) Public relations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advertising">Advertising<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advertising" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ Refers to drawing attention to or describing a product in a public medium e.g. newspapers, radio, television e.t.c
✓ Any advert in order to give value for its purpose should contain the following aspects.</p>
<p>i) a media presentation
ii) payments for the advert
iii) Identifiable sponsor who pays for the advert. Note:</p>
<p>✓ Any communication without costs to the sponsor is publicity and not advertisement.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="advertising-media">Advertising Media<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advertising-media" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>✓ An advertising media is the means through which an advertised message is conveyed to the members of the public who are consumers.
✓ The following are some of types of media available to advertisement. The press e.g. newspapers, Posters, Billboards, Brochures, Shopping news, Radio, Television, Neon signs e.t.c</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="factors-which-determine-choice-of-an-advertising-medium">Factors which determine choice of an advertising medium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-which-determine-choice-of-an-advertising-medium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>a) The intended target group
✓ The nature of the target group in terms of habits customers age, e.t.c will determine choice of the right medium.
b) the physical characteristics</p>
<p>Page 43 of 165

<p>✓ The mediums physical characteristics i.e visual aspects, colour, movement's e.t.c. c. Media circulation
✓ Where an advertiser aims to reach countrywide cliental, choice of a nationwide media is necessary.</p>
<p>c) Cost of advertising
✓ Should be affordable and that they should be reasonable compared to the returns.
d) Urgency of the advertisement
✓ Urgent and quick adverts may require mediums such as Radio, TV e.t.c</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sales-promotion">Sales Promotion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sales-promotion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Sales promotion refers to the strategies and incentives which are aimed at promoting the purchase of a given product.
✓ The sales promotion strategies include; i) gifts and other premiums e.g soap, toothbrushes ii) discounts iii). displays e.g supermarket iv) credit facilities. Use of loss leaders – one good is sold cheap to attract customers. vii. Use of free samples viii). After sale services.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-publicity">b) Publicity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-publicity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Refers to the free advertising whereby the desire for a product is created or boasted by unpaid – for features or presentation in the mass-media ( e.g a feature in press)
✓ These features may be solicited for or unsolicited for but remain entirely unpaid for by the business. – or a news release sent to studio.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-public-relations">c) Public Relations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-public-relations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The term public relations (PR) when used in product promotion refers to the process of communicating information of an organization product, Policies and actions to specific consumer groups or the public at large.
✓ This is done with the view of creating awareness and a positive attitude towards the organization and the product.
✓ It could also be done to correct mis-information or rehabilitate a spoilt image in order to get a satisfied client.
✓ It aims at creating a favorable attitude towards the organization in order to promote acceptance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-4-factors-which-may-influence-an-entrepreneur-in-choosing-a-promotional-method">3.4 Factors which may influence an entrepreneur in choosing a promotional method.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-4-factors-which-may-influence-an-entrepreneur-in-choosing-a-promotional-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>cost element of each method of promotion should be analyzed in order to suit financial abilities</li>
<li>Targeted audience is important in order to address an appropriate combination method.</li>
<li>The nature of the product to be promoted i.e those that may require demonstrations and training et.c</li>
<li>Urgency of the promotional message.</li>
<li>Availability of resources especially the mechanical physical and human resources to implement a promotional mix.</li>
<li>Level of demand for the product; where demand is high fewer promotional methods are required</li>
<li>the competitors promotional strategies</li>
<li>availability of media that is most accessible to its customers</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="organizational-forms">ORGANIZATIONAL FORMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organizational-forms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unincorporated-business">Unincorporated Business<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unincorporated-business" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These are business which do not have separate entity (existence from that of their owners)</li>
<li>According to law such organizations are one and same in the existence of the owner.</li>
<li>They do not have separate rights and obligations from those of their owners</li>
<li>They include</li>
<li>i) sole proprietors</li>
<li>ii) partnership</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sole-proprietorship">Sole Proprietorship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sole-proprietorship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sole means single while proprietorship refers to the owner of a business owned by one person who takes responsibility on risks of the business.</li>
<li>He either enjoys the profits or servers the losses of the business alone.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="formation-of-sole-proprietorship">Formation of Sole Proprietorship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#formation-of-sole-proprietorship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is simple and easy to form since legally only licensed from the government is required</li>
<li>If the name of the business is different from that of the owner the business name should be registered with the registrar.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-sole-proprietor">Management of Sole Proprietor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-sole-proprietor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The owner of the business is the manager of the business</p>
<ul>
<li>He makes decisions operating the day to day activities the business.</li>
<li>He may employ people to work in the business or be assisted by family members. <strong>Sources of Capital</strong></li>
<li>The term capital is used here to refer to the resource required to start and operate the business</li>
<li>He may obtain capital from; i) his own savings ii) borrowing from friends and relatives iii) banks and other financial institutions iv) credit suppliers v) borrowing from government institutions i.e. KIE, ICDC vi) funding from non-government organizations vii) hire purchase funds viii) The business itself from retained profits.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="liability">Liability<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#liability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Liability refers to the extent which the owner of the business can be called upon to meet the debts of the business.</p>
<ul>
<li>A sole proprietorship is viewed as being one and the same with the owner hence does not have separate rights and obligation.</li>
<li>Where a sole proprietorship business cannot pay its liabilities all its assets and the business properties are sold in order to clear the business debts.</li>
<li>The responsibility of the owner of the sole proprietorship business is thus unlimited.</li>
<li>The sole proprietor is therefore said to have unlimited liability.</li>
</ul>

<p>This means that the liability of the owner is no just restricted to capital contributed but extends to include its personal property.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="features-of-a-sole-proprietorship">Features of a Sole Proprietorship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#features-of-a-sole-proprietorship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Is a business owned by one person</li>
<li>It had no separate legal existence from its owner</li>
<li>It has a limited legal life since its existence depends on the life of the owner.</li>
<li>The owner has unlimited liability in the business.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-a-sole-proprietorship">Advantages of a Sole Proprietorship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-a-sole-proprietorship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>It is easy to start since only a license is required</li>
<li>Quick decision making</li>
<li>Freedom of action at any time</li>
<li>Flexibility in adopting quickly to changes in customers needs</li>
<li>Profits are entirely on the owner’s hands</li>
<li>There is control over business secrets</li>
<li>Easy to use family labor cheaply.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-sole-proprietorship">Disadvantages of Sole Proprietorship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-sole-proprietorship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Limited life in case of death of the owner</li>
<li>Unlimited liability may cause the owner to loosing personal property.</li>
<li>The sole proprietor serves loses entirely by himself</li>
<li>Limited capital may delay expansion.</li>
<li>working for longer hours may result to fatigue</li>
<li>Lack of essential skills may cause mis-management.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="circumstances-under-which-the-sole-proprietorship-ideal">Circumstances under which the Sole Proprietorship ideal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#circumstances-under-which-the-sole-proprietorship-ideal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>When customers show preference to specialized services</li>
<li>Where small capital is required to start up a business</li>
<li>Where returns are low and may not warrant ee existence of a large business.</li>
<li>Where the market experiences frequent demand changes</li>
<li>Where locations are remote and the population may be small.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dissolution-of-a-sole-proprietorship">Dissolution of a Sole Proprietorship<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dissolution-of-a-sole-proprietorship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Dissolution refers to the termination of the legal existence of the business.</p>
<p>This may be caused by;</p>
<p>i) The death of the owner
ii) The transfer of the business to another person.</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Problems the Sole Proprietorship may face.</p>
<ol>
<li>Lack of continuity in case of death.</li>
<li>Lack of skills may lead to mis-management</li>
<li>Working for longer hours may lead to fatigue</li>
<li>Loses are served by the owner</li>
<li>Limited capital to facilitate expansion functions.</li>
<li>Lack of consultancy may lead to poor decision making</li>
<li>Unlimited liability may cause lose of property.</li>
</ol>
<p>4.1.2 Partnership</p>
<p>☑ According to the partnership Act. A partnership is referred to as a relationship which subsists between persons carrying on a business in common with view of making profits.
☑ A partnership is thus an extension of sole proprietorship and is in fact necessitated by the fact that a sole trader may for several reasons fail to carry out his business efficiently and profitability.
☑ Partners pull the financial and managerial skills together in order to make profit.</p>
<p>Formation</p>
<p>☑ According to the partnership Act (934) a partnership business may come into existence through any of the following ways.</p>
<p>i) Orally
ii) By actions of persons concerned iii)
By a simple put in written iv)
By a partnership deed</p>
<p>NB the above ways of forming a partnership are allowed by the partnership Act, However its better to remember that it may be made illegal under the following circumstances.</p>
<p>Circumstances under which the Partnership is illegal</p>
<p>☑ If the partnership has been formed for an illegal purpose e.g. theft.
If is formed and the partners do not meet the minimum qualifications e.g. auditing</p>
<p>☑ Where the partnership contains more than 20 members</p>

<p>☑ Where the partnership wants to run their business with the name which does not disclose the true names of all the partners or the name had not been registered under the registration of the business Act under which it is deemed illegal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="requirements-for-the-registration-of-a-business-name">Requirements for the Registration of a Business Name.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#requirements-for-the-registration-of-a-business-name" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Under the partnership Act, the partners must furnish the registrar of business names for the following</p>
<p>a) The business name
b) The general nature of the business
c) The principle place of location of the business
d) The present Christian and sir names together with their usual residential address.
e) The nationality of each partners
f) Any other occupation of the partners
g) The date of commencement of their business.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-partners">Types of Partners<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-partners" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="a-general-partners">a) General partners<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-general-partners" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>☑ These are the real partners in new sense of the partners which refers to those partners who are the most active partners in the partnership
In most cases the general partner is a reliable of the debts of the partnership. b) Limited partners</p>
<p>☑ This is a partner whose liabilities are limited to the amount of capital contributed to the partnership business
☑ This type of partners do not usually participate in the management of the partnership becas4 if thy do they loose their limited liability in respect to the transaction and decisions participated in.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="c-active-partner">c) Active partner<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-active-partner" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>☑ This is the type of partner who takes the active part in the running of the business.
In most cases such a partner may be employed somewhere or may be in another business all together</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ The partner contributes capital to the partnership business and the profits or losses at lower proportions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="articles-of-partnership-partnership-deed">Articles of Partnership/ Partnership Deed.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#articles-of-partnership-partnership-deed" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Although it is not a statutory requirement the partnership can be formed by a written agreement, it is usual for the partnership business in particular those involved in huge commitments to write articles of a partnership also known as a partnership deed.
✓ The aim of this document is to safeguard the interest of each partner and it constitutes a legal contract among the partners.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contents-of-a-partnership-deed">Contents of a Partnership Deed<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contents-of-a-partnership-deed" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>The capital and property of the firm together with the respective capital contributions of each partner.</li>

<li>The rules as to the case of interest on capital and drawings by partners. 5. Provision for proper accounts and their audit</li>
<li>The power of each partner.</li>
<li>The drowns for the resolution of the partnership</li>
<li>The method of determining the value of good will on retirement of drafting in of a new partner.</li>
<li>The method of determining the amount payable to a deceased partner.</li>
<li>No partners may should carry on a competing business</li>
<li>Any changes in partnership composition must be agreed upon by all partners.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-partnership">Management of Partnership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-partnership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ Members of a partnership are correctly responsible for the management of the business.
✓ The members may share responsibilities and duties according to their respective skills and availability in order to ensure effectiveness in management of the partnership.</p>
<p>The partners may decide to hire skilled or non-skilled labour to assist the management of the partners.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="features-characteristics-of-a-partnership">Features/ characteristics of a Partnership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#features-characteristics-of-a-partnership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Mutual agency – each partner is an agent of the partnership and therefore any action by one partner with transacting the business binds the rest of the partners provided his actions are within the partners express or implied authority.</li>
<li>Limited life- since the partnership is a relationship originating from an agreement between two or more members any changes in their relationship caused by factors such as- death withdrawal of a partner e.t.c terminates the partnership or dissolves it.</li>
<li>Unlimited liability
☑ In a partnership the partners' liability is not limited to the amount of capital investment.
☑ The partners are separately held liable for the debts of business and their personal properties may be sold to meet such debts.</li>
<li>Ownership of interests – the interest of a partner in a partnership business e.g. right to inspect the accounting records of a firm of a firm, admission or dismissal of partner transit of interest e.t.c must have the full consent of the partnership.</li>
<li>Sharing of profits</li>
</ol>
<p>Each partners share of profits of proportional to his/her investment in the partnership. And any agreement of non-partner to share the profits does not make a non-partner a partner.</p>
<p>NB circumstances under which a non-partner may be included in sharing the partnership profits and losses.</p>
<ol>
<li>As compensation for services rendered to the partnership</li>
<li>As compensation for the partnership use of his/her property or name. 3. As payments for loans advanced to the firm 4. As payment to the next of kin.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sources-of-capital-of-a-partnership">Sources of Capital of a Partnership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-capital-of-a-partnership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>contributions from partners</li>
<li>Loans from commercial banks and other financial institutions</li>
<li>Stock from hire purchase firms</li>
<li>Credit facilities from suppliers</li>
<li>Loans from government institutions e.g. K.I.E e.t.c.</li>
<li>Plough backs from retained profits</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-partnerships">Classification of Partnerships<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-partnerships" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are five ways through which partnership are classified.</p>
<ol>
<li>By trading</li>
</ol>
<p>A partnership may be classified was</p>
<p>a) Non-trading partnerships- these partnerships whose activities are to offer services e.g. legal, medical, accountancy, teaching e.t.c.
b) Trading partnerships – these are partnerships whose main activities are manufacturing, purchasing or sales of goods.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>By liability</li>
</ol>
<p>a) General partnerships – are partnerships in which all partners may publicity act on behalf of the firm and each partner individually be held responsible for the debts of the firm. Their properties may be attached to clear the debts of their partnership.
b) Limited partnerships – a partnership whose activities of certain partners are limited. The personal liabilities of such partners (limited partners) are limited to a certain amount stated. These amounts are normally equivalent to the amount of their contributions.</p>
<p>NB the following conditions must be fulfilled for a limited partnership to be formed.</p>
<ol>
<li>The partnership should not consist more than 20 partners.</li>
<li>The partnership must consist one or more general partners.</li>
<li>The limited partners are not liable to the partnership debts beyond his capital contribution.</li>
</ol>
<p>NB Restrictions of the limited partners.</p>
<ol>
<li>Is entitled to inspect the books of the firm and examine the partnership state at any time.</li>
</ol>
<p>Page 51 of 165
This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>The death, withdrawal bankruptcy of a partner shall not cause dissolution of a partnership or the partnership can not be dissolved by a court order because of lunacy of the partner.</li>
<li>A limited partnership is only dissolved by the general partners unless brought through a court order.</li>
<li>Any differences on partnership matters can only be decided by a majority of the general partners.</li>
<li>With the consent of the general partners a limited partner may assign his/her shares in the partnership to another person.</li>
<li>A person may be introduced into the partnership without the consent of the limited partners.</li>
<li>By time duration</li>
</ol>
<p>a) A temporally partnership (joint venture partnership) – this is a partnership formed for a specified period of time</p>
<p>☑ Termination of the stated period or accomplishment of the purpose may cause the partnership to come to an end.</p>
<p>b) a permanent partnership (partnership at will) – This is a partnership formed to carry the business indefinitely</p>
<p>☑ It does not have a fixed life of fulfilling its purpose</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>By activity</li>
</ol>
<p>☑ a) Active partner – this is a partner who is actively involved in the day to day management of the partnership and may be paid a salary for these services. And the partner is held liable for the debts of the firm.</p>
<p>b) A dormant /sleeping partner – does not take part of the day to day management of the partnership but contributes capital, shares profits and is liable for the business debts</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>By capital contributed</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>a) Real partner – a partner who contributes capital into the business and whose name may be used in relation to transactions of the business and enjoys the profits of the partnerships.
b) Nominal partner – is a partner who has not contributed any capital to the business but allows his or her name to be used in the business. They are usually influential persons whose names can be used.</p>
<p>☑ He is not fully liable to the partnership debts however is he presents himself to the public in a manner that portrays him a general partner he will be held liable.
c) Quinsy-partners – a partner who has retired from the partnership but has left his capital in the partnership business which is treated as a loan, he earns interest</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-by-age">6. By age<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-by-age" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Majority partner – A partner who has attained the age of 18 years and above. Such a partner unless stated to the centrally can be held liable for the partner.
i) Partner shares only profits and not losses since he didn't participate in decision making that may have caused such losses.
ii) The liability of the minor is limited only to the amount of capital contributed to the business since any liabilities arising may not be part his decision making.
iii) The minor partners can act on behalf the partnership and such acts shall be binding on the other partnership iv) When the minor partner attains the age of majority he/she has up to six months to decide whether or not to continue with the partnership. If he/she decides to stay, he has full responsibilities and rights of a major partner.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="termination-dissolution-of-partnership">Termination/ Dissolution of Partnership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#termination-dissolution-of-partnership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Although the partnership deed or articles of partnership will contain regulations of terminating the partnership, nevertheless in the absence of our subject these regulations, a partnership may be dissolved in the following ways.</p>
<ol>
<li>When the fixed time if any are stated in the articles of the partnership expires.</li>
<li>If the partnership was specifically entered into for a given venture, transactions or undertakings the completion of which or achievement will automatically dissolve the partnership.</li>
</ol>

Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>If the partnership is a partnership at will, it can be dissolved by any partner giving notice of his intention to dissolve the partnership.</li>
<li>By mutual consent of all partners</li>
<li>By bankruptcy or death of one the partners.</li>
<li>By one partner’s shares in the partnership being changed or attached by a court order for private debts.</li>
<li>If any events occur which will make the partnership business illegal, the partnership will stand dissolved irrespective of the content of the partnership deed.</li>
<li>Automatic or compulsory dissolution as it is provided section 39 of the partnership Act which lay the following grounds under which a partnership may be dissolved by a court order.</li>
</ol>
<p>i) If any one of the partners becomes insane ii) If any of one partner becomes permanently incase of performing his/her duties through in capabilities, accidents or disabilities iii) Where a partner has acted in a manner which is pre-judicial to the carrying out firm’s business and may bring the name of the business to its disables.</p>
<p>iv) Where a partner was found guilty of breach the partnership contract. v) Where the firm has been operating in losses.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="circumstances-under-which-the-partnership-deed-is-ideal">Circumstances under which the Partnership Deed is ideal.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#circumstances-under-which-the-partnership-deed-is-ideal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>In a business where the amount of capital required is reasonably large.</li>
<li>If professional were pulling together effort for efficiency and better performance.</li>
<li>If professional areas where the law prohibits a couple of days.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-operating-a-business-under-a-partnership">Advantages of Operating a Business under a Partnership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-operating-a-business-under-a-partnership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>A partnership business benefits from the talents of individual ensuring almost efficiency and acceptance.</li>
<li>Since a partnership would be owned by a no. of partners it sets a basis of pulling together saving to raise large capital for investments</li>
<li>Sound decision making through consultative processes</li>
<li>A higher growth rate as a result of combining ambitious from different partners.</li>
<li>Partnerships have a good will and financial influence enabling it to raise finance easily.</li>
<li>Collateral or security of loans can be easily be raised.</li>
</ol>

<ol start="7">
<li>Formation of partnership business requires minimal government interventions.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-operating-a-business-under-a-partnership">Disadvantages of Operating a Business under a Partnership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-operating-a-business-under-a-partnership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Slow decision making due to long discussion processes</li>
<li>Sharing of profits tends to disregard hard working partners.</li>
<li>Partnership business have limited life incase of retirement or dead of one partner.</li>
<li>Disagreements make partnerships business vulnerable to disputes among partners.</li>
<li>The partners have unlimited liability which lead to loosing personal property in the event the partnership business cannot settle its debts.</li>
<li>The agency burden where every partner is an agent of the partnership and one’s partner’s mistake may affect the rest.</li>
<li>Limited managerial skill may lead to mismanagement of the business.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-2-incorporated-business-joint-stock-companies">4.2 Incorporated Business / Joint Stock Companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-2-incorporated-business-joint-stock-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="i-incorporated-business">i) Incorporated Business<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-incorporated-business" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>We have so far looked at unincorporated business and have seen the main features of such business is that they do not have a separate legal existence from the owners.</li>
<li>We shall now focus on business units that are legally viewed as separate and distinct units from their owners</li>
<li>Such businesses are called in co-operated or joint stock companies.</li>
<li>Incorporated business organizations are legally separate and distinct from their owners or members.</li>
<li>The main forms of incorporated business or joint stock company include;</li>
</ul>
<p>i) Companies
ii) Co-operative societies
iii) Public co-operation</p>
<ul>
<li>These are advanced forms of companies where a group of people pull their savings together and contribute as capital to set up a business enterprises or companies.</li>
<li>These companies are governed by Acts of parliament under the Kenya all joint stock companies fall under the Kenya Companies Act = (cap 486) of 1948</li>
</ul>

<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> This is a process that creates an organization separate and distinct from the person forming it (owners)
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The organization is known as a body corporate and registered company is known as a cooperation</p>
<p>NB companies are business organizations or units formed to carry out a specific activity.</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> They are organized by processing an existence that is separate and distinct from the persons who own it.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> Companies have rights and obligations of a natural person.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rights-and-obligations-of-companies">Rights and Obligations of Companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rights-and-obligations-of-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>It can own and dispose of property.</li>
<li>It can enter into a contract on its own name</li>
<li>It can borrow and lend money in its own capacity</li>
<li>It can hire and fire employees</li>
<li>It can sue and be sued in its own right</li>
<li>It can form subordinate agencies and its authority</li>
<li>It can spread information.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="features-of-a-company">Features of a Company<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#features-of-a-company" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is an artificial person created through legal process
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> A company has rights and obligations of natural person e.g. holding and disposing property.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> A company has a perpetual life independency of the owners lives i.e. has perpetual succession.</p>

<p>✓ A company has a separate legal identity from the owner. ✓ A company is created for a particular purpose
✓ The owners of a company enjoy limited liability</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-companies">Types of Companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ There are basically two types of companies. Namely
a) Public limited companies
b) Private limited companies</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="public-limited-companies">Public Limited Companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#public-limited-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ A public limited company has a minimum number of 7 members with no maximum membership.
✓ The maximum membership normally is determined by the number of authorized shares (capital) of the company
✓ In Kenya a public limited company has the term limited at the end.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-features-of-a-public-limited-company">Characteristics/features of a Public Limited Company.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-features-of-a-public-limited-company" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Minimum membership is 7 with no maximum</li>
<li>Invites members of the public to subscribe to its shares</li>
<li>The shares are easily transferable among shareholders</li>
<li>It has a minimum of 3 directors</li>
<li>It has authorized minimum capita figure.</li>
</ol>
<p>NB authorized share capital is to the total shares that have been legally authorized by the government during the company’s registration</p>
<p>✓ A public limited company starts to operate after receiving a certificate of commencement (trading)</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-private-limited-company">A private Limited Company<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-private-limited-company" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ This is a company with a minimum of 2 persons and a maximum of 50 persons excluding all past and present employees.
☑ A private limited company should have name ending with limited.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-a-private-limited-company">Characteristics of a Private Limited Company.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-a-private-limited-company" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Has a minimum of 2 members and maximum 50 members</li>
<li>It does not invite the members of the public to subscribe its shares.</li>
<li>It’s shares are not easily transferable unless with consent with other share holders.</li>
<li>Operates with only one director.</li>
<li>Its shares don’t have authorized minimum capital figure. It can start its operations after receiving its certificate.</li>

<p>This is the fact that the liability of companies of owners is restricted to the amount of investment of a company plus any other amounts that to be undertaken to be contributed towards payment of one companies debt.</p>

<p>i) Shares
ii) Guarantee.</p>

Public limited companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-public-limited-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>i) The aim is to safeguard the interests of public investors

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-private-limited-companies">2. Private limited companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-private-limited-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ These companies are formed by submitting the necessary requirement to the registrar of companies (the five documents)</p>
<p>Once this has satisfied the registrar of companies such a company will receive a certificate of incorporation.</p>
<p>☑ The private limited companies are usually not allowed to advertise their shares to attract public money and as such they sell their shares privately (private placing to the interested members of the public.
☑ Like public limited companies, private limited companies have limited liability, their shares are not fully transferable as they are not quoted at the stock exchange.
Any transfer of shares requires the consent of other share members of the company.</p>
