<p>☑ Advantages of a Company</p>
<ol>
<li>More capital can be raised since it has large membership</li>
<li>The company offers better collateral for loans to be advanced.</li>
<li>Limited liability secures private property incase of inability to pay debts.</li>
<li>The companies have continuity i.e. have perpetual life or succession.</li>
<li>A company has a liability to hire highly qualified professionals facilitating better management</li>
<li>Shares are easily transferable.</li>
<li>The companies have legal identity and therefore no conflicts to its members.</li>
</ol>
<p>Disadvantages of a Company</p>
<ol>
<li>Difficult to form since it is costly and has long legal procedures</li>
<li>The company has restricted operations by the memorandum of association</li>
<li>Slow decision making due to long approval procedures</li>
<li>Limited ownership caused by land of control of the firm</li>
<li>The agency burden may cause mismanagement when especially the board is weak.</li>
<li>Double taxation especially of the dividends</li>
<li>Lack of secrecy since the company has to publish its financial status annually.</li>
</ol>
<p>Main Features of Joint Stock Companies</p>
<p>☑ As already noted a joint stock company is an association of people who contribute capital to form common stock in order to carry on a business activity for product motive.
☑ The company formed comprises- corporate status and is registered under the company’s act.
☑ A joint stock company may be public or private company and its main features include;
a) Legal personality – the company has identities separates from that of other persons contributing capital and can therefore hold property, contract in its own name sue and be sued.</p>
<p>b) The shares are transferable – the share holders can sell their interest in the companies to other persons willing to invest in it (freely for public ltd company but limited to the consent of the rest of the shareholders for private company.</p>
<p>c) Common sill – as a separate entity it will be necessary for a joint stock company to sign documents and such signatures are normally embodied in a common sill of a company.</p>
<p>✓ The sill is kept under custody of the responsible offices.</p>
<p>d) Members/ shareholders can not bind the company by their Acts</p>
<p>e) Individual/ members are not entitled to take part in business since it is managed by the board of directors</p>
<p>f) Shareholders have a limited liability.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-joint-stock-companies">Advantages of Joint Stock Companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-joint-stock-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>The liability of share holders is limited to the capital contributed by shares guarantee.</li>
<li>A joint stock company is going concern implying that it has perpetual existence separate from that of the shareholders.</li>
<li>A joint stock company is an artificial legal person independent of the shareholders and it can own its assets and liabilities.</li>
<li>The shares of a joint stock company in particular public limited company are freely transferable.</li>
<li>The shares of a joint stock company can easily be used as security for loans making it easy to obtain loans.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-joint-stock-companies">Disadvantages of Joint Stock Companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-joint-stock-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ It lacks secrecy and privacy since it requires audited financial statement annually.
✓ The formation of a joint stock company requires long legal formalities.
✓ They are difficult to form since they require a heavy capital investment.
✓ Joint stock companies can not increase their capital investments beyond the legally authorized capital.
✓ The decision making process of joint stock company is slow and bureaucratic due to consultations.
✓ Joint stock companies are not flexible to changes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dissolution-of-a-joint-stock-company">Dissolution of a Joint Stock Company<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dissolution-of-a-joint-stock-company" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>✓ When a company has started its expected to continue with its operations to the future since it is a form of business with perpetual succession.
✓ Termination of the life of a company may be through;</p>
<ol>
<li>Failure to commerce business within one year of its formation – upon this it may be would up by its court order on application.</li>
<li>The membership falling below the required minimum and this dissolution may be decided by a court order.</li>
<li>Accomplishment of the purpose or expirely of the period of operation.</li>
<li>The registration if it fails to comply with statutory cooperation e.g failure to file annual files to the registrar of companies or engaging in illegal activities.</li>
<li>A resolution by members to voluntarily wind up the company which may arise through.;
a) where the company does not have a future on that line of business
b) The members wish to sell it as a going concern in order to share profits.
c) Where one company is acquired by another and the members wish to discontinue it so as to terminate its existence a separate legal entity.</li>
<li>Through a merger with a larger company</li>
<li>Insolvency – the company is not able to meet its obligations.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="holding-companies">Holding Companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#holding-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ The company Act of the laws of Kenya defines a holding company as one which has more than half of equity share capital of another company of which it is a member or controls a bigger percentage of the board of directors of one or more other companies which are called subsidiary companies.
✓ A holding company may be public or private depending upon wishes of the promoters or shareholders.
✓ In Kenya a good example of a holding company is ICDC.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-3-public-corporations">4.3 Public Corporations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-3-public-corporations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ This is the net price to which the government has stakes in
✓ The government owns a certain percentage of the enterprises shares.
✓ Where a government has a fall ownership of the corporation, the business enterprise is known as a parastatal
✓ Some public corporations are profit seeking while other are not.</p>

<p>✓ examples of such public corporations include: Kenya pipeline Kenya airways KCB (Kenya commercial Bank) Kenya lighting company (KPLC)
✓ Parastatals are run to provide the essential services such as education, medical etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="similarities-between-public-cooperation-s-and-joint-stock-companies">Similarities between public cooperation's and joint stock companies.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#similarities-between-public-cooperation-s-and-joint-stock-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>✓ They are both legal entities
✓ They are governed by a board of directors appointed ✓ They are self financing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="public-corporations">Public corporations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#public-corporations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>A cooperation is wholly and partially owned by the government</li>
<li>Corporations tend to be monopolists</li>
<li>Are operated on public interest not entirely on profit motive.</li>
<li>They are paid for by the public from the taxes collected by the government.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="joint-stock-companies">Joint stock companies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#joint-stock-companies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Owned by the public and has shareholders.</li>
<li>They are subjected to companies</li>
<li>Purely operate on a profit motive.</li>
<li>Private funds finance joint stock companies.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="parastatal-bodies">Parastatal Bodies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parastatal-bodies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A parastatal body is an organization distinguished from a body government but in which the government is a sole owner.</p>
<p>✓ They are established by the government to perform specific functions and their management is in the hands of board of directors.
✓ The board of directors is appointed by the government and the parastatals bodies do not sell shares since they are whole financed by the government.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="marketing-boards">Marketing Boards<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marketing-boards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These are produce organizations set up to encourage and control of the Agricultural produce.</li>
<li>Their objective is to protect producers and consumers and may be formed by both producers coming together or be constituted by the government.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-marketing-boards">Classification of Marketing Boards<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-marketing-boards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>commodity marketing boards- these are producer organizations with objectives are restricted to purchasing and selling of commodities e.g coffee, tea, pyrethrum</li>
<li>producer marketing boards- this is a produce organization dealing with a wide range of products e.g maize, wheat e.t.c</li>
<li>Expert marketing boards- this concentrate on marking one or more products overseas e.g KTDA or coffee board.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-marketing-boards">Functions of Marketing Boards.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-marketing-boards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>To encourage and control the marketing of Agricultural produce through purchasing at fixed prices to facilitate stable incomes</li>
<li>To encourage income and price stability through the buffer stock in buffer funding system.</li>
<li>To facilitate farmers to obtain loans for farm inputs e.g quality fertilizers, seeds and equipment.</li>
<li>To support the government in licensing regulations</li>
<li>To provide a wide range of sport e.g transport, grading, packaging of products e.t.c</li>
<li>Marketing boards provide advisory advise to farmers</li>
<li>They facilitate research on agricultural products and markets.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="formation-of-a-public-cooperation">Formation of a Public Cooperation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#formation-of-a-public-cooperation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ They are formed by a specific Act of parliament which define and powers and the overall mandate of their institutions.
☑ The law creating corporations also state the minimum capital under which they will operate.
☑ The corporations are viewed as separate legal entities and may be wholly or partially owned by the government.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-public-corporations">Management of Public Corporations.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-public-corporations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ This is under a board of directors.
☑ The directors are appointed by the government when the government owns wholly the corporation or relevant joint directors and government appointed directors where the government owns partially the cooperation.
☑ The government influences decisions of the corporations either directly or indirectly e.g. pricing decisions.
☑ In Kenya the board of directors is appointed by the relevant ministries or by the president.
☑ It is this board which is responsible for the implementation of the policies of the organization.
☑ The board may employ professional managers charged with the day to day running corporations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sources-of-share-capital">Sources of Share Capital<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-share-capital" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Public corporations may get their capital from the government through loans or budgetary provisions.</li>
<li>Where the government owns corporations jointly both contributions of capital and the public will raise capital through issuing shares.</li>
<li>As a body corporate a public corporate has power to borrow money from financial institutions.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="features-of-a-public-corporation">Features of a Public Corporation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#features-of-a-public-corporation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>A service motive- they provide essential services to the citizens and may therefore not aim at making profits – entirely.</li>
<li>They are formed by an Act of parliament which states that government ministries will take charge of such corporations.</li>
</ol>
<p>Page 70 of 165</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>They are subsidized by the government to enable them to provide essential goods and services at minimum fees.</li>
<li>The board of directors is wholly appointed by the government or jointly with other stakeholders to influence the policies of the cooperation.</li>
<li>They are financed by the government but for jointly owned public corporations.</li>
<li>It has a legal distinct from the government or any other owners</li>
<li>They have limited liability</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-public-corporations">Advantages of Public Corporations.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-public-corporations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Raising initial capital is each since funds comes from the government</li>
<li>Public corporations improve the welfare of the people since basic goods and services are offered at affordable prices</li>
<li>The company has limited liability</li>
<li>They are used to meet government objectives.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-public-corporations">Disadvantages of Public Corporations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-public-corporations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Political influence may lead to a weak management</li>
<li>Public corporations may not respond to consumer needs since some operate as monopolist.</li>
<li>Public corporations have a public interest making them difficult to achieve their objectives.</li>
<li>The job insecurity of senior managers e.g. C.O.S, may lead to dishonest management</li>
<li>Slow decision making because of the size of same public corporations</li>
<li>most corporations are loss making</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dissolution-of-public-corporations">Dissolution of Public Corporations.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dissolution-of-public-corporations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ Since formation of a public corporation is by an Act of parliament it follows therefore, that in order to dissolve such an organization one would have to repeal the Act of parliament under which they are allowed.
☑ The following reasons may lead to repealing the Act of parliament under which they are formed.</p>
<ol>
<li>Perpetual operations of the corporation of a loss</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on
5
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Outright insolvency.</li>
<li>Mismanagement which mat adversely affect the performance of the corporation</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-4-co-operative-societies">4.4 Co-operative Societies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-4-co-operative-societies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ This refers to a co-operative.
☑ The term co-operative is derived from cooperation
☑ It is a body of people or a body of persons who have agreed to come together to achieve a certain goal.
☑ The members of the public get together to voluntarily contribute capital to the corporate society sharing the risks of investments in order to achieve and enjoy the benefits.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reasons-for-promoting-cooperative-societies-in-kenya">Reasons for Promoting Cooperative Societies in Kenya.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reasons-for-promoting-cooperative-societies-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ They facilitate members to manage their own society and distribute themselves the benefit generated.
☑ In order to increase bargaining power in selling the members produce or gaining maximum satisfaction.
☑ In order to enhance participation by members in economic activities minimizing the middlemen.
☑ In order to reduce market cost of produce especially in transportation and storage.
☑ In order to promote and improve quality production
☑ In order to facilitate stable income earning
☑ In order to put together capital resources of expensive investment e.g. transport, refrigeration e.t.c.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="formation-of-co-operative-societies">Formation of Co-operative Societies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#formation-of-co-operative-societies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>☑ They are formed by a minimum number of 10 members who pursue to undertake some objectives
☑ The members work out a defined plan of what the co-operative society is supposed to do. For the co-operative society to be formed they have to submit their constitution to the commissions of co-operative societies with the following detail.</p>
<p>☑ The objectives of the society
☑ By-laws of the society</p>

<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The co-operation then recruits members who pay registration fees and buy their specified shares in the society.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> No member is allowed to buy more than 5% of the share capital.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The registration of the co-operative society makes it a body separate meaning it becomes a separated entity distinct from its owners and with perpetual succession.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ownership-and-management-of-a-co-operative-societies">Ownership and Management of a Co-operative Societies.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ownership-and-management-of-a-co-operative-societies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> It is owned by its owners and its ownership and membership is opened and voluntarily
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The members in a co-operative society have a limited liability to the amount contributed.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The supreme authority of the registered co-operative society is in the AGM (Annual general meeting).
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> During the AGM the managing director is elected on one person one vote basis irrespective of the shares owned by each member.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The outcome is determined by a simple majority and such elections are supervised by the district corporation officer.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The managing director serves for a period of time after which elections are held by a vote.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The elected members hold constant meetings to discuss operations and the concerned of the cooperative.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> The committee may employ professional staff to charge of various parts in the society.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span> A number of sub-committees may be formed from the elected officers to take to take various responsibilities of various societies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="examples-of-committees-in-a-co-operative-society">Examples of Committees in a Co-operative society<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examples-of-committees-in-a-co-operative-society" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Executive Committee- The committee is charged with the day to day running of the society and its membership is made up of the following</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Chairman
b) V-chairman
c) Honorable secretary</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>d) Treasurer</p>
<p>e) Secretary</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Education committee- It is charged with educating members of the society and it is made up of 3-members answerable to the executive.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Credit committee- It is normally common in saving and credit societies. It is made up of 3-members answerable to the executive and it is charged with the following:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>i) Processing loan applied and making recommendations.</p>
<p>ii) Loan recovery</p>
<p>iii) Credit recommendations and approval</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Supervisory committee- It is charged with overseeing the overall management of the society's finances.</li>
</ol>
<p>The Relationship between the Cooperative Society and its Business with its Members</p>
<p>☑ A cooperative society should usually transact its business with its members.</p>
<p>☑ This business relationship relates the following relations.</p>
<p>i) The customer relations- The members can be customers of the cooperative society by purchasing its goods and services</p>
<p>ii) The supplier relations- The members can supply to the society by the seeking to the cooperative society marketing their produce.</p>
<p>iii) The employee relations- The members can be employees who work for the cooperative society which they jointly own.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-capital-for-cooperative-societies">Sources of Capital for Cooperative Societies.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-capital-for-cooperative-societies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Members contributions through</li>
</ol>
<p>i) Registration fee</p>
<p>ii) Amount contributed by members to purchase shares</p>
<p>iii) The fee charged from the proceeds or sales of the members produce.</p>

<p>iv). Interest earned on money loaned out or firm inputs advanced to members.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>The loans from financial institutions.</li>
<li>Plough backs or financing through retained profits.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="features-of-the-cooperative-society">Features of the Cooperative Society<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#features-of-the-cooperative-society" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Separate entity- Registration of a cooperative society makes it separate from its owners and the cooperative society has rights and obligations that are separate distinct from those of its owners.</li>
<li>Liability-The liability of its members is restricted to the amounts they have contributed in terms of capital.</li>
<li>The minimum membership of a cooperative society is 10 persons and the maximum number is specified since it depends on the share capital of the society.</li>
<li>Continuity-The cooperative society has a perpetual life.</li>
<li>Cooperative societies are governed using by-laws contained in the constitution of the cooperatives.</li>
<li>The share capital is divided into units both persons who want to become members of the society.</li>
<li>The cooperative society is run by management committee elected</li>
<li>The distribution of profits to the members is according to the level of activity carried out among members-High volume of activity command high portions of profits.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="essentials-for-the-success-of-a-cooperative-society">Essentials for the Success of a Cooperative Society.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#essentials-for-the-success-of-a-cooperative-society" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Adequate volumes to secure the benefits of large scale production.</li>
<li>Adequate finance to fund operations construction purchasing of equipments.</li>
<li>A sound management team with effective entrepreneur skills.</li>
<li>Existence of a definite objective</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-cooperatives">Principles of Cooperatives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-cooperatives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Open Membership</li>
</ol>
<p>Membership is open and voluntary without artificial restriction imposed on membership</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Democratic administration.</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The affairs of the cooperative society are managed in a democratic manner and elections are on a one person</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Service to members- The primary purpose of a cooperative society is to render services to members.</li>
<li>Distribution of profits or surplus- Distribution of profits or surplus is based on a specified rate.</li>
<li>Limited interest on capital- This is because the aim of cooperative society is to help its members and not make profit.</li>
<li>Cooperation with officer cooperative society so as to achieve a common purpose and a common objective.</li>
<li>Education to its members.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-cooperative-societies">Types of Cooperative Societies.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-cooperative-societies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A cooperative is a voluntary association of persons who come together to promote their social economic interest.</p>
<p>The types include:-</p>
<p>a) Producer cooperatives</p>
<p>A producer cooperative is an association of producers such as societies which collect, process, market and distribute the members produce.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-producer-cooperatives">Functions of Producer Cooperatives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-producer-cooperatives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) Getting better prizes for members produce.
ii) Providing better transport facilities for moving the produce from the source to the market.
iii) Providing better storage facilities for members for members produce. iv) Proving grading, packing and processing services to the members. v) Extending credit facilities to its members.
vi) Educating members on better methods of production through seminars, demonstrations etc.
vii) Facilitating use of quality seeds, fertilizers and farm inputs</p>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Page 77 of 165</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="consumers-cooperatives">Consumers Cooperatives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#consumers-cooperatives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A consumer cooperative is an association of borers who have the same consumer needs.</li>
<li>The consumers buy bulky and sells to the consumers at lower/fair prices.</li>
<li>This reduces the cost of products by eliminating the middle men.</li>
<li>The main function of these cooperative societies is to purchase and distribute quality goods to members at reasonable prices.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="benefits-of-the-consumer-cooperatives">Benefits of the Consumer Cooperatives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#benefits-of-the-consumer-cooperatives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>i) They make goods easy available to members.
ii) They buy goods in bulky and sell to members at lower prices. iii) They distribute the realized profits to members at lower prices</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="why-consumer-cooperatives-are-not-popular-in-kenya">Why consumer cooperatives are not popular in Kenya.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-consumer-cooperatives-are-not-popular-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Fears competition between the local traders which push prices down and provide quality goods hence no need for cooperatives.</li>
<li>Many people supply enough subsequent food for themselves.</li>
<li>Most people cannot afford large amount of capital required to start.</li>
<li>Most population in Kenya lives in the rural setup and may not accept the cooperative rule.</li>
<li>No proper attention to such cooperatives by the government.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="savings-and-credit-cooperative-society-saccos">Savings and Credit Cooperative Society (SACCOS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#savings-and-credit-cooperative-society-saccos" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These societies are formed by persons who come together to save their money in a common pull with a view of getting loans to improve their welfare.</li>
<li>The members of a SACCO are usually under one employer and members contributions are deducted from their salaries but the employer to the cooperative society through a check of system at regular intervals usually monthly.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>At the members savings earn interest and get loans at reasonable interest rates normally 1% per month.</li>
<li>Members savings serves as a security for a loan, three guarantors and a pay slip.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-saccos-are-popular-among-employees">Why SACCOs are Popular among Employees<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-saccos-are-popular-among-employees" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) It is easy to save with the SACCO since deductions are done through a check of system.</p>
<p>i) Easy to get loans from SACCOs due to fewer simple requirements.
ii) Interest charge on loans is low compared to commercial banks.
iii) Loans do not require collateral except for members' salary slip and guarantors.
iv) Members savings are save since they are insured.</p>
<p>v) In case of death the beneficiaries do not lose their savings in cooperatives nor they are called upon to repay.
vi) SACCOs are flexible since they give different types of loans e.g. normal, emergency, school fees loans, medical etc.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="structure-of-cooperative-societies">Structure of Cooperative Societies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structure-of-cooperative-societies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This refers to the hierarchy of the cooperative movement.</li>
<li>It shows the various levels of which various cooperatives operate this include:
i) Primary Cooperatives</li>
<li>Draw membership from business organizations engaged in production of particular goods and services.</li>
<li>Such cooperatives are found in specific geographical, turgid or sector.</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples: - Local agricultural societies in different regions.</p>
<p>ii) Secondary cooperatives made up of the primary cooperative within a region e.g. a district. Through such cooperative the primary cooperative society pulls their objectives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="main-reasons-of-forming-a-cooperative-union">Main Reasons of Forming a Cooperative Union<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#main-reasons-of-forming-a-cooperative-union" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To strengthen the buying capacity especially of farm inputs or transport facilities.</li>
<li>To negotiate for loans for members cooperatives from the cooperative banks.</li>
<li>To market the produce of members cooperatives.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>To help members cooperatives with the processing of their produce.
To help member’s cooperatives with storage, administrative services, accounting etc.
To educate, advice, train, the staff of members cooperatives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="national-union">National Union.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#national-union" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This is the union of various cooperative unions.</li>
<li>The national cooperatives form umbrella bodies of cooperatives formed.</li>
<li>The membership of such a cooperative comprises cooperative societies or operating in a particular production line.</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples:-
a) The Kenya Planters Cooperative Union.
b) The Kenya Union of Savings and Credit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="apex-cooperatives">Apex Cooperatives.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#apex-cooperatives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are the overall cooperative bodies to which all other cooperatives i.e primary, cooperative unions and national union are carried. An example in Kenya is the Kenya National Federation of Cooperatives Union. They are formed to promote cooperative performance with the aim of:-
a) Providing information about the activities of cooperative in Kenya.
b) Providing education and training for member cooperative for efficient and
c) Represent Kenya cooperatives both regionally and internationally.</p>
<p>Another example is the Kenya cooperative bank.</p>
<p>iii) International cooperatives: Are composed of national cooperatives from various countries
e.g. The Kenya Federation of Cooperatives</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="problems-facing-cooperative-societies">Problems Facing Cooperative Societies.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#problems-facing-cooperative-societies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Mismanagement by cooperative officials who take advantage of their knowledge and position to benefit themselves.</li>
<li>Unskilled management elected without any knowledge whatsoever with management skills.</li>
<li>Lack of adequate capital due to small contributors and difficult to get bank loans.</li>
<li>Capital interference and self interests.</li>
<li>Most cooperatives are agro based facing price fluctuations climatic problems, low prices etc.</li>
<li>Little government input to rejuvenate the cooperative societies.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="advantages-of-cooperative-societies">Advantages of Cooperative Societies.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-cooperative-societies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Low cost services to members.</li>
<li>Improved welfare of members enhancing their participation in economic activities.</li>
<li>Encourage savings enabling members to accumulate their capital.</li>
<li>Extended credits to members at low interest rates improving their welfare.</li>
<li>Limited liability protecting personal property.</li>
<li>Flexibility in membership for entity and exit.</li>
<li>Equality of the members in terms of rights irrespective of the number of shares held.</li>
<li>Large capital base due to high membership.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-cooperative-society">Disadvantages of Cooperative Society<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-cooperative-society" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Poor management caused by the system of choosing the managers I.e. AGM elections.</li>
<li>Constant political interference causing unrest and mismanagement.</li>
<li>Withdrawals are easy which may cause instability and discontinuity.</li>
<li>Slow decision making due to over consultation.</li>
<li>Lack of secrecy since all activities must be approved by all members.</li>
<li>Large membership may cause management problems.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dissolution-of-a-cooperative-society">Dissolution of a Cooperative Society<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dissolution-of-a-cooperative-society" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Disagreement among members or an agreement of members may lead to application of registration.</li>
<li>Insolvency- Where the cooperative is unable to meet its debts.</li>
<li>By a court order upon application by one or more members.</li>
<li>An order of dissolution by the apparent ministry in the interest of its members.</li>
<li>Withdrawal of members leaving membership to less than the minimum required.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chapter-five">CHAPTER FIVE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-five" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-0-resource-needs-for-entrepreneurship">5.0 RESOURCE NEEDS FOR ENTREPRENEURSHIP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-0-resource-needs-for-entrepreneurship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this lecture we shall discuss the sources of business finance which include equity finance, debt finance – loan, bills of exchange, factoring, trade debtors, accrued expenses, credit card buying (plastic money), debenture finance, invoice discounting (confidential factoring), factoring, sale and lease – back, sale of an asset, and purchase.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-objectives">General objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of the course the learner should be able to identify the appropriate sources of funding for entrepreneurship. At the end of this lecture you should be able to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Explain the Various sources of finance for entrepreneurship</li>
<li>Discuss the advantages and disadvantages of the various sources of finance</li>
<li>Identify factors that influence the various sources of finance sought</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5-1-sources-of-business-finance">5.1 Sources of Business Finance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-1-sources-of-business-finance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ The entrepreneur may obtain finance from the following main sources.</p>
<ul>
<li>Debt financing</li>
<li>Equity financing</li>
<li>External and internal sources.</li>
</ul>
<p>☑ Debt financing requires a borrowing system and the entrepreneur is bound to pay back the funds borrowed together with interest payable.
☑ Debt financing can be long term or short term. Depending on the lender collateral, amy be required.
☑ Equity financing does not require collateral and offers the investor some form of ownership position in the business.
☑ Internal financing are funds generated from several sources within the company, they include profits sale of Assets, reduction in the working capital accounts receivable, retained profits e.t.c
☑ External sources of finance may come from family members, credit suppliers, government programmes, grants e.t.c.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5-1-1-equity-finance">5.1.1 Equity Finance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-1-1-equity-finance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ It the largest source of finance to a business organization and usually forms the base of which other finances are raised.
☑ Equity is the total sum of the business ordinary shares plus the retained earnings also known as revenue reserves.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-ordinary-share-capital">a) Ordinary share-capital<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-ordinary-share-capital" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It that finance contributed by ordinary shareholders of a business. It is raised through the sale of the company's ordinary shares- who are the real owners of the business.</li>
<li>The finance type is only raised by limited companies and is permanent in nature and can only be refunded in the event of liquidation.</li>
<li>It earns ordinary dividends as a return to the investments.</li>
<li>The investors carry voting rights and usually each share is equal to one vote.</li>
<li>The ordinary shares are quoted at the stock exchange where they are sold and bought.</li>
<li>The finance carriers the highest risks in the company because it gets its return after other finances have got their and also in the event of liquidation is it paid last.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on

Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The ordinary dividends are not a legal obligation on the part of the company to pay.</li>
<li>Where the profits are good ordinary shareholders get the highest return because their dividends are varied.</li>
<li>This type of finance grows with time and this growth is equity which basically is facilitated by retention earnings.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advantages-of-ordinary-share-capital-to-shareholders">Advantages of Ordinary Share Capital to Shareholders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advantages-of-ordinary-share-capital-to-shareholders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ordinary shares have a right to vote and their votes influence the company’s activities.</li>
<li>Ordinary shareholders can use their shares to secure loan.</li>
<li>Ordinary shares are easily transferable.</li>
<li>The owners of the ordinary shareholders earn dividends in perpetuity.</li>
<li>The fluctuating nature of dividends is earned.</li>
<li>The ordinary shareholders benefit from the residual claim in the event of liquidation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="disadvantages-of-ordinary-shareholders">Disadvantages of Ordinary Shareholders.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disadvantages-of-ordinary-shareholders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Carry variable returns in case of low or non-profit dividends are not paid..</li>
<li>Incase of liquidation an ordinary shareholder may lose everything.</li>
<li>The sale of more ordinary shares dilutes ownership of the existing shareholders.</li>
<li>The dividends of an ordinary shareholder are double taxed.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-retained-earnings-revenue-reserves">b) Retained earnings (revenue reserves)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-retained-earnings-revenue-reserves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ This is a source part of equity finance which arises out of undistributed profits over and above dividends paid to shareholders</li>
<li>☑ It is a cost free source of finance and its cost is opportunity cost in terms of foregone dividends to ordinary shareholders.</li>
<li>☑ The retained earnings constitute growth in equity which is a cost of equity because the company may declare retained earnings as extra dividends or inform of bonus issues.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="arguments-in-favour-of-retention">Arguments in Favour of Retention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arguments-in-favour-of-retention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Acts as a stabilizer to future dividends (ordinary dividends) especially when profits perform poorly.</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by PATRICK NGOBIRO (<a href="mailto:patrickngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">patrickngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>2 No cost are incurred for it's acquisition
3 It is able to be raised at no notice especially during unforeseen events e.g.
a. Abrupt increases in the prices of raw materials
b. Fire hazards e.t.c
4 Promotes savings promoting investments and growth.
5 Large volumes of retained earnings influence the company's shares positively.
6 A good source of finance to those very urgent short-term ventures whose returns are immediate
7 The boost the company's creditability to the company's creditors.</p>
<p>The advantages of using retained earnings as a source of finance to the company.</p>
<ol>
<li>It is the largest internal source of finance which the business will use without paying any costs.</li>
<li>The use increases the equity base of the company making it possible to generate more debt finance.</li>
<li>Retained earnings are used to finance new fixed assets whose value cannot be met by other sources</li>
<li>It is used without pre-conditions or restrictions making it the most flexible source of finance.</li>
<li>It boosts confidence among the company's creditors</li>
<li>It is a permanent source of finance to the company to be used on long-term investments.</li>
</ol>
<p>The disadvantages of using retained earnings as a source of finance to the company.</p>
<ol>
<li>Easily misused by the management as it may be invested in areas which are prejudicial to majority shareholders.</li>
<li>Retained earnings once used will leave not shield to take care of contingencies exposing the company.</li>
<li>The finance can easily be mis-invested in areas of quite low returns.</li>
<li>the source involves a lot of sacrifice to the ordinary shareholders inform of opportunity cost</li>
<li>Easily invested in high risk investments.</li>
</ol>
